Earth Sphere, Episode 1
is the first scenario in the Earth Sphere section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders II: The Wizard's Throne
.
Story
Gabriel is gone. I can no longer feel his power in me.  I entered the Wizard's Throne Room.  Gabriel said nothing.  He pointed to the sphere of earth.  I wanted to help him.  I wanted to fight the circle of traitors that mounted this attack against him, but he forbade me.  Even to the end he believed this quest would work. With his last spark of power he forced me through the sphere of Earth, deep within this world. Gabriel's presence is gone.  The conspirators have taken the Wizard's Throne.
This was their design all along.  Their movements on the Blessed Continent were diversions as they crept over Evermore, securing the necessary towers to overpower Gabriel. Without Gabriel I cannot return to Evermore, and cannot complete my quest. I am doomed to wander in these caverns. This earth is my grave. With the power of the Throne in villainous hands, nothing in this world can endure.
—Merlin's opening monologue
Map features
Wizards
Merlin
- The player begins at the southeast of the underground with no cities
Mab
(CPU Lord) - Mab begins with her main city at the northeast of the underground, but also has other cities on the map, including on the surface
Fangir
(CPU Knight) - Fangir begins in the southeast part of the underground
Notable structures
Ancient Ruin
- Near the center of the underground level, north of Grimmoch (the first friendly Dwarf city that will join Merlin)
2x Ancient Ruin
- North side of the area on the surface
Haunted Crypt
- South side of the area on the surface
Dragon's Lair
- South side of the area on the surface
Magic Vault
- Near the lava lake outside of Fangir's area
Magic Vault
- In the lake in the northeast area of the underground accessible by tunneling. This vault has a fixed reward of providing the Rift Lord summon spell.
Items
An item bag is located east of Merlin's starting position
An item bag is located north of Merlin's starting position, in a dead-end corridor that also contains an earth node and a mine
An item bag is located north of Mab's main city, in an area that is accessible by tunning (since the area has a beetle belonging to Mab, it is possible for Mab to collect the item or tunnel this area using the beetle)
Heroes
Grogmir
(Dwarf rogue) - Independent hero at Grimmoch who will join at no cost, along with his stack and the city
Danah
(Goblin shaman) - Starting hero for Mab
Tengar
(Dwarf rogue) - Starting hero for Fangir
Walkthrough
In the beginning, Merlin must perform a slow dungeon crawl while not having any cities. While the underground tunnels in the starting area have various places to explore, the relevant path is northward, and then eastward at the four-way intersection.  From here, traveling further east, avoiding the area marked by Goblin warning signs, and then south will get Merlin to the first Dwarf city of Grimmoch, which provides the hero Grogmir at no cost.
From Grimmoch, traveling further east will get to Fangir's Halls. Fangir is a friendly wizard who will typically offer an alliance during the scenario. Securing an alliance with Fangir mitigates Merlin's starting disadvantage against Mab. The entrance to Fangir's Halls east of Grimmoch also has a very useful exit to the surface, which offers town and resources. With Fangir as an ally, the only opponent that needs to be defeated is Mab.
This map has a secret area in the northeast part of the underground level that can be accessed by tunneling through a 1-hex earth barrier. Tunneling can be done by a Dwarven Mole or a Goblin Big Beetle, both of which have the Tunneling ability. In order to tunnel, the Mole or Beetle must be in a stack on its own (or in a stack without any units that lack Tunneling). This secret area contains several gold mines, as well as a magic vault with the Rift Lord spell.
Outcome
I am learning to appreciate the ways of the Dwarf and Earth. Dwarves work among forges. It is a strong symbol, reminding me that I must remain true to Gabriel's vision, despite the heat. Like the Dwarves I must invent a new solution.
The tunnels of stone hold many mysteries, including one wizard who has been strangely detached from the fighting on the surface world. This death wizard, may know how I can complete Gabriel's quest.
—Merlin's closing monologue

Walkthrough
The player begins with a very modest position compared to Arachna's, but rapid expansion is very rewarding due to the large number of structures and items on this map. Optimal expansion paths involve an area marked to the south of the starting area, where there is a sign that reads "Passage out of the underground." This sign also entails an ambush by spiders. Immediately to the northeast of the sign is a Goblin city that can be taken. A more valuable location, however, is further south, which leads to another sign. There is a cave exit to the east, but this exit is perhaps not the most useful. Instead, proceeding further south and then southwest leads to another cave exit. The above cave exit leads to the surface at the west side of the map.
The west side of the surface map has a camp and the Dwarven outpost that will join for free. There is also a teleport in the area, which takes you to the east side of the surface map, where, further northeast, there is a large Dwarven city that will join for free. Taking these two Dwarven holdings, as well as the Goblin city mentioned above provides a strong early position against Archna for the rest of the scenario.
Arachna's underground dungeon has a network of magic relays, all of which are traps that will teleport your stack to the spiders nest at the southeast of the underground. You can leave this nest by finding a neutral Mole, which has the Tunneling ability to dig out of the nest. The nest has three item bags and a Magic Vault that may benefit the player.
Outcome
Arachna has surrendered, but she refuses to support my cause. She thinks she can hide from the new Wizard's Throne. Her followers hate Evermore, and will not go there. I suspect she is afraid.
Still, she has given me access to the Hallowed Halls, the burial ground for Elves. It is a sacred place for the Dark Elves. All Elves are immortal and should never die, but many died in this world, and thus Dark Elves exist. If I am to learn anything about death, it will be in the monument forged by Human violence.
—Merlin's closing monologue

Earth Sphere, Ep. 3

Earth Sphere, Episode 3
is the third scenario in the Earth Sphere section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders II: The Wizard's Throne
.
Story
The Dwarves have forged many items, but nothing quite so grand as a sword of great power, said to unite warring factions. It is probably a legend, but if such a sword did exist, it would be useful.
Dwarves love riddles, stories and myths. I don't know if I can trust them, but this sword is said to be hidden in the ancient forges near a place called Deepmir. It is said to be able to cleave stone. I will search for this sword hidden in stone.
—Merlin's opening monologue
Wizards
Merlin
Mab (CPU King)
Tempest (CPU King)
Yaka (CPU King)
Nimue (CPU King)
Walkthrough
There are four King-level hostile wizards, but they are also at war with each other, making the objective of this scenario easier. The Deepmir sword is located in the lava area directly west of Deepmir, and is guarded by a phoenix. Deepmir itself can be reached from the cave entrance next to Yaka's main city, or from the cave north of Nimue's main city. The Deepmir sword itself gives +2 attack, +2 damage, +2 resistance, and Magic Strike. Picking up the sword with any hero or teleporting it to any hero will complete the scenario.
This scenario can also be completed by defeating all other wizards. However, that if you complete the scenario in this manner, the sword will not be in the inventory of any hero from this section of the campaign that might appear in the campaign finale.
Outcome
The sword is indeed marvelous. I am not sure how it will assist me, or if it has any power over the minds of people, but I am intrigued by the Dwarven legends. I will remember them, and perhaps they will serve me, if not now, then in some future age.
—Merlin's closing monologue

Earthquake

Earthquake
is the first scenario in the Dwarves route of the
Keepers version
of the
campaign
in
Age of Wonders
, and the fourth scenario in the campaign overall. Earthquake and the rest of the Dwarves route are available only if the player chose to help the Dwarves following the conclusion of
United Cities
.
Story
Earthquake
Rumors abound as Dwarves ooze from the wounded mountains. Though reluctant to speak to me--a stranger--I have overheard talk of gnashing earth releasing hoards of nastiness. From what I can gather, there are many survivors still trapped below and the city of Delatar is vulnerable, overrun by refugees and exposed without Deepmir. If predators lurk among the labyrinth, I shall hunt them. The Dwarves gave me use of a trained Giant Mole, and I am ready to enter, to assist in any way I can. Delatar must be strengthened if the Dwarves hope to avoid obliteration.
About the Dwarves
The Dwarves are a stubborn, reclusive folk. Because many of their secrets are stolen and used for destruction, Dwarves tend to keep to themselves. Even Keepers know few hard facts about the Dwarves, save that they are honorable. Fiercely industrious, Deepmir Dwarves employ complex machines to create and defend their home. Their larger cities are capable of building many contraptions, including airships and cannons. They are gentle and are known to befriend Giants and other strange creatures. Their smallest outposts can enlist zealous berserkers with a special round-attack, which delivers a blow to multiple enemies.
IN-GAME TEXT
Map features
Starting positions and cities
Dwarves
(player-controlled) - The player begins at the upper middle of the surface level with no cities.
Goblins
(
CPU Squire
) - The Orcs have their main city, Garneth Depth, at the south section of the caverns level.
Orcs
(CPU Knight) - The Goblins occupy cities in both the caverns and depths levels. Their main city is Cairn at the east part of the caverns level.
Notable structures
Castle Ruins
(average item value) - West section of the surface north of the river
Castle Ruins
(average item value) - Near the Orc main city of Garneth Depth at the far south section of the caverns level
Dungeon

(average prisoners value) - Northeast section of the depths
Arena
- At the northwest corner of the map
Wizard tower
(level 2 Special spell) - Southeast corner of the region south of the river
Heroes
Bandir the Fiery
-
Free hero
(Dwarf) - As a free hero, Bandir is eligible to emerge if the player has at most one hero besides the leader, given that this map has a hero limit of 2. However, emergence is random and is not guaranteed. The next guaranteed opportunity to recruit a hero will be in the 6th scenario of the campaign (
Hall of Heroes
).
Jattah the Leper
(Goblins)
Doktok the Fat
(Orcs)
Sister Tersia
(Goblins)
CPU Leaders: Protier (Goblins), Argrad (Orcs)
Walkthrough
Earthquake is arguably the most complex map in the entire campaign in terms of pathfinding, with maze-like lower layers that take a great deal of time to explore. The player begins with two units that can perform
tunneling
, namely a
Drill
and a
Dwarf Mole
. Tunneling is necessary to progress in the underground levels, and further add to the complexity of the map (for information on how to use tunneling, please see the above-linked ability article).  The player is also given
builders
, which can be used to restore razed cities encountered in the underground.
The most natural approach at the beginning is to travel down the initial cave entrance to reveal an area with mines and razed cities reachable by tunneling. From this point on, heading northwestward reveals the size 3 Goblin city Gug. The path SE from Gug leads to the Goblin leader at Cairn and enables the Goblins to be defeated early in the map. Additionally, south of the initial caverns area is a downward cave entrance that leads to the ruins of Deepmir, which can be rebuilt with the use of a builder.
Since this map has numerous Goblin cities, building favorable
race relations
with Goblins can potentially be worthwhile, especially if the
Tranquility
spell is available. The surface is potentially valuable, since it has a large number of independent cities and is generally safer than the underground due to the small number of access points that enemy units can take. Besides the initial cave, there are only two other exits from the underground to the part of the surface north of the river, both of which are on the east edge of the map. Note that Dwarven units have
mountaineering
, which enables them to cross mountains on the surface. The size 4 independent human city of Nimand, located to west of this map's starting position, can be reached by crossing the mountains.
Reaching Delatar
The objective is to reach (and occupy) Delatar, which is located at the southeast corner of the map's surface level. Routes to Delatar include the following:
Via the northwest section of the caverns
- The NW section of the caverns can be reached by tunning south and then west from the initial cave entrance. This part of the map features the size 4 city Pelack. From Pelack, you may either use the cave adjacent to the city or the teleport to the southwest.
Cave route
- Travel directly south in the depths level, eventually crossing a lava bridge. After the lava bridge, there are three caves that lead upward to the west section of the caverns. The closest cave is marked by the sign "
Cavern to the Dwarven cities Bezulath and Darname
," which takes you to a location just south of Bezulath (a size 4 city with a moat and three bridges). After taking this cave upwards, travel southeast to reach the exit to the surface. This and other possible routes are shown in the walkthrough maps in the "Gallery" section below.
Teleport route
- After taking the teleport, head south and then northwest to reach the same area just south Bezulath as described above. Then, travel southeast to reach the exit to the surface.
Tunneling
- From Pelack, it is also possible to tunnel to the west section of the caverns by tunning the west edge of the map. If the scenario has played for a long time and the AI possess tunneling units, this route may already have been tunneled.
Via the surface and the depths
- If you reach the northeast exit to the surface, it is possible to eventually reach the southeast cave on the surface, which leads back to the caverns level. From here, traveling downward to the depths and then westward within the depths will arrive at a cave up to the caverns level. This path converges to the teleport route described above.
Tunning the depths around Deepmir
- If you take the cave down to Deepmir, tunneling immediately further to the south or in other directions outward from Deepmir will open routes that converge to one of the routes described above.
Via the south section of the depths
- A very unlikely route without advance knowledge of the map, the south section of the depths can also be reached from the central and east sections of the same level by traveling over water/lava stream or by tunning the southeast corner of the depths level. The south section of the depths leads to the Orcs' main position, which has an exit very close to Delatar, as well as another exit at the SW section of the caverns.
Crossing the main surface river
- It is also possible to reach Delatar via the surface by flying over the river with flying units, or crossing the river with other means, such as with the use of
Water Walking
. The river crossing is guarded by hostile independent
Red Dragons
, but there is a gap in the dragon line directly south of the size 4 city Nimand that can be flown through safely.
Shortcut method
- If
Eagle Riders
or other flying units are carried over from the previous map, it is possible to fly south through the gap to reach Delatar early on.
Delatar is an independent Dwarven city that will, under ordinary circumstances, offer to join the player when it is reached. Despite the story premise of this scenario, it is not necessary to reach Delatar before the Orcs do. However, if the Orcs capture Delatar, they will likely migrate the city to the Orcs and eventually use it to produce Red Dragons, which may threaten cities on the surface that you may have taken.
Outcome
No Accident
Unlike Orc captives, intimidated Goblins speak freely of their orders. The Cult of Storms had foreknowledge of the collapse, and secreted forces into the mountains to be ready to pounce, "when rocks chattered like teeth." Surviving Dwarf stone-sayers claim the sudden shift in fissures could not happen. Yet, the Cult of Storms knew it would? It was no accident. Still, Delatar is currently safe, though vulnerable and taxed by its burgeoning population of destitute outcasts. My only comfort is the tenacity of these exiled. They refuse to accept defeat, and strengthen my resolve in our cause.
IN-GAME TEXT
Gallery
Walkthrough map of the caverns level
Walkthrough map of the depths level
Deepmir as depicted in this scenario

O'neron Scenario 1: Eastern Pass
is the first scenario in O'neron's section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders: Shadow Magic
.
Story
Once a powerful Dwarven outpost, the land has turned to wasteland. The battles destroyed most cities and scarred nature. Still, many dwarven tunnels remain where a few survivors still cling to life.
Aye, O'neron, it has begun. The Shadow Demons are moving faster than they ever have, hungrily tearing at the fabric of reality, but they cannot do so without paying a price.  What took millennia to complete on your world threatens to swallow this one in weeks.
I have sent Teryn to find the source of the Demons' power. I feel it, tearing through me. So much pain and magic. Hard to focus... despair not. This is not your world. We shall not allow it to happen again. O'neron, we need you.  Rescue as many as you can, help is coming.  Your people, they come. Find refugees, and survive, until I can tell you where you must go to stop this nightmare.
—Merlin's intro
Map features
Wizards
O'neron (Player) - The player begins at the northwest with no cities
All-Devourer (CPU Lord) - The All-Devourer has cities across the map. Additionally, he has a city in the corner of shadow realm that has a one-way teleport to the surface, but cannot be reached by the player by any means.
Items
Item bag (Helm of Light) - Southwest part of the underground
Heroes
Ector (Syron warrior) - Starting hero for O'neron
Belendor (Human warrior) - Independent hero who will offer to join when met at the road in the beginning
Quall (Shadow Demon rogue) - Starting hero for the All-Devourer
Aerul (Syron priest) - Hero who will offer to join at the end of the scenario
Walkthrough
The initial goal, given by Teryn is to find the refugees who have made a stronghold underground. To reach the refugees, travel east along the road, recruiting the Human hero Belendor, and then south from the city being destroyed by the Shadow Demons. From here, there are two paths to the underground. One path is to cross the river and follow the road to a cave entrance. The other path is to head south, eventually going off-road to find another entrance.
Upon arriving in the underground, the refugee stronghold, which includes three cities, is found at the northwest part of this level. Here, you can steadily build up your forces, since the entrance to refugee area is guarded by a watch tower located at a chokepoint that can only be attacked from one adjacent hex, while also allowing defenders to be placed from the rear hex. This means that a few strong defensive units will make it possible to defend the watch tower and the rest of the refugee area.
After arriving at the underground stronghold, the next task, also given by Teryn, is to reach the Dwarven city of Rumborg, located at the southeast part of the surface. Once you've built up enough forces to expand outward and reach the city of Romsborg, Syron forces will begin arriving in the next few days. Eventually, a third hero, Aerul, will arrive and offer to join. After Aerul arrives, the scenario automatically completes on the next turn.
Outcome
Your spirits are high. The Forceships whisked away the refugees. I sense your joy in seeing your Syron people again. I have little time. The void is closing in around me, while energy shreds my soul. I came here to learn of the enemy, and I think I found something, but I fear the All-Devourer desires my soul. He knows of my trick.
Teryn hides. She should be safe, but, with his attention upon me, I cannot resist the voices much longer.  Watch yourself, O'neron. Look to the East. Go toward the Sunbirth Mountains, through the Shadowlands.
—Merlin's outro
Notes
The map file for this scenario has an unused internal map name of "Fear no Evil."

Evermore
is the final scenario in the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders II: The Wizard's Throne
. In this scenario, Merlin returns to
Evermore
to claim the Wizard's Throne and to save
Julia
from
Inioch
.
Story
Merlin, hear me! This moment in death, the very cosmos quakes; I can reach to you from beyond the void and warn you.
Inioch stirs.  The Dark Lord of Death rises again.
Desperate to return to the Ancient Ways, the rebel wizards sacrificed the Wizard's Throne to entreat Chaos itself. Inioch seduced them.  From the Valley of Wonders he enticed them with obscene dreams.
He lies. Inioch will tear asunder all creation to rid the world of the Age of Men and reform the world into something that never existed.
Inioch's daughter, Julia, is the vessel he inhabits.  Inioch will consume her.  She decays in his embrace. Only you can save her. Rid this world of Inioch.
Merlin.  You have learned each sphere, now master the Sphere of Cosmos.
My friend, you must forget me. Go now, out of death.
It is yours now, Merlin.
Claim the Wizard's Throne!
—Gabriel's opening monologue
Map features
Wizards
Merlin
- Merlin begins near the central teleport ring with no units and no cities
Julioch
(CPU King) - "Julioch" is the in-game name of the wizard that is Inioch's possession of Juila. Julioch begins at the center of the map, in possession of the Wizard's Throne. Similar to Juila, Julioch commands the Elves and is a Life Sphere wizard. Julioch and all other wizards begin at peace with one another.
Yaka
(CPU Emperor) - Yaka starts at the southwest section of the surface. Although Yaka is not the main antagonist of this scenario from a story perspective, he is an Emperor-level opponent, whereas Julioch is only a King-level opponent.
Nimue
(CPU Lord) - Nimue starts at the northeast section of the surface
Serena
(CPU Lord) - Serena starts at the northwest section of the surface
Mab
(CPU Lord) - Mab starts in the south section of the underground
Nekron
(CPU Lord) - Nekron starts at the southeast section of the surface
Tempest
(CPU Lord) - Tempest starts at the north section of the surface
Heroes
Heroes are acquired in this scenario only through a special game mechanic, as described in the walkthrough section below.
Walkthrough
At the beginning, the Spirit of Magic will inform the player how to use the central teleport ring. Essentially, this ring is a series of teleports that can take Merlin to 6 different nodes, corresponding to each sphere of magic. Each node is a teleport. Stepping on the node will take Merlin to a corresponding part of the map for the selected sphere.
Summoning heroes
After stepping through one of the six node-teleports, Merlin must capture a nearby city independent that serves as a "trigger city" for summoning the highest-level hero that was acquired for the corresponding sphere during the course of the campaign. There are a total of 6 trigger cities on the map (one for each sphere), each located near a corresponding node-teleport destination. However, the node-teleports are one-way teleports, meaning that you will need to visit other trigger cities by traveling to them on the map, or by traveling back to the center and using another node-teleport. Each node-teleport can only be used once. Trigger cities do not need to be captured by Merlin specifically, if there are other units available for the task.
Although there are 6 trigger cities, Merlin can summon his previous heroes from at most three spheres, one for each opposing pair of magic spheres (i.e., Air-Earth, Fire-Water, and Life-Death are opposing spheres). When Merlin summons a hero from one magic sphere, the wizard of the opposing sphere will receive the highest-level hero that was acquired by the player during the campaign for that opposing sphere. For example, if you capture the trigger city for the Air Sphere, you will receive the highest-level hero that you acquired during the Air section of the campaign, while Mab (the wizard for the Earth Sphere) will receive the highest-level hero that you acquired during the Earth section of the campaign. Therefore, some of the heroes that you developed during the campaign will join opposing wizards, and may need to be fought in this scenario.
The 6 trigger cities are:
Norlith (Air) - A Frostling city located at the north edge of the map, northeast of Tempest's starting position
Elmshire (Water) - A Halfling city located at the east edge of the map, in between Nimue and Nekron's starting positions
Boktor (Fire) - An Orc city located in the southwest part of the map, east of Yaka's starting position and near a Dragon's Lair
Palatus (Life) - An Archon city at the northwest part of the map, north of Serena's starting position
Miranor (Death) - A Dark Elf city in the southeast part of the map, southwest of Nekron's starting position
Drumbor (Earth) - A Dwarf city located south of the map's center and north of the larger independent Dwarf city of Masaland
Normally, you can only summon one hero (the highest-level hero) from a particular sphere. However, there is an exploit in that if you lose control of the trigger city, recapturing it again will summon another hero from that sphere, specifically the second-highest-level hero of that sphere (or the third-highest-level hero, etc., if the process is repeated). This exploit can be performed using one of the following methods:
Give the trigger city to another wizard through the diplomacy interface, and then recapture it back. In order for the city to be in the list of structures that can be offered, the other wizard must have a unit close to the city. Sometimes, the other wizard will not accept a plain offer of just the city; in this case, offer something else (such as free mana) together with the city.
Allow a hostile unit to take trigger city, and then recapture it back.
Raze the trigger city and rebuild it using a pioneer. This will count as recapturing the city.
Completing the scenario
Other than the hero summoning system described above, this scenario plays as a typical domination game that requires defeating all other wizards. Note that merely defeating Julioch and taking the central city is not enough; all other wizards must be defeated as well, with allied victory disabled. At the start of this scenario, Merlin loses access to all previously researched spells, and must start his spell research all over, this time in the Cosmos sphere. The Cosmos sphere includes most (but not all) spells that are associated with the six standard magic spheres.
Outcome
Victory is mine. From the Wizard's Throne I have the power to restore Julia and cast out Inioch.  I feel it now-that other power. It freed Meandor's soul from a life of hatred. It preserved Julia's soul from a dark end. And it brought my people back from their demise. It is the fury in war and the structure of peace. Elusive as it may be, I see it as I gaze upon Julia's still face and bend to its majesty.
—Merlin's closing monologue
Quotes
"
Do not fear, I shall look after my treacherous daughter, and give her the existence she so richly deserves. You shall be spared the sight of your world falling into Chaos, for I, Inioch, have risen, and I bring forth your doom!
" —Julioch (message to Merlin at the start of the scenario)
Notes
Capturing a trigger city can spawn a hero that joins a wizard who has already been defeated. When this occurs, the spawned hero will simply stay in place without moving. It is not necessary to defeat such hero in order to complete the scenario.

Facing a Legend
is the 4th scenario in the Orc route in the
Cult of Storms version
of the
campaign
in
Age of Wonders
, and the 7th scenario in the campaign overall. The backstory of this scenario is depicted in
Hall of Heroes
scenario in the
Keepers campaign
. The image used in the opening story text is also the same as that of Hall of Heroes.
Story
True Legends
Am I the only Stormlord of ability? As I prepare for the next great battle, I received word that Melenis has been routed. The Dwarves have destroyed her forces and are providing shelter to the Halflings that I drove from the United Cities. The Stormlord, Melenis, is dead. Meandor is livid. She was his favorite. She was my favorite. She will be missed. These Keepers will suffer for her loss. I will see to that. Even as we approach Bormac, rumors abound in camp. It makes me laugh that Bormac must use lies to bolster his presence.
The news of Melenis has shaken the faith of my followers. Stormlords are regarded as immortal. No doubt, Bormac has had a hand in disseminating the rumor of her demise among my children. He must be desperate. Having spent a century trapped away from the world has made him weak. Things have changed since Bormac lived, and while his legend has grown, so have I. It is time I extinguished this blasphemous Keeper mythology for the good of the Cult. No longer will they be scared stupid by such tales.
IN-GAME TEXT
Map features

(player-controlled) - The player begins at the southwest corner with only a single size 1 city. The player is at war with all other factions, which are all neutral to one another.

Walkthrough
The player starts small and must defeat multiple opponents that have a large number of cities. Getting to the Lizardmen and Dwarven cities will require crossing the sea either by water or via two underground passages that respectively begin at the north and the southeast edge of of the southern landmass. The Dwarves are a King-level opponent, which is relatively strong at this stage of the campaign. Fortunately, the number of cities that the Dwarves control will likely be limited by the Lizardmen, especially if the two factions do not go to war with each other.
After completing this scenario, the player must then choose between joining the Dark Elves or the Undead. This selection will direct set the campaign's endgame faction.
Outcome
Immortality
I am all that remains, immortal. Bormac is dead, and the Orcs celebrate. They wrestle over campfires, and break tables under the stupor of sour wine. All about, the Orcs brawl, savoring the spoils of this victory. Tomorrow I will face Meandor and receive the progress of all the other Stormlords. I already know the outcome of the meeting. The other Stormlords will come with excuses, while I will deliver these new children to Meandor and start again with a new prospect. I grow weary of their mediocrity. Once the Orcs were as these Stormlords, but no more.
Stars of Rebirth
Blood of rebirth soaks the star over the Valley of Wonders, and only I look to the bright symbol without trembling. I never thought Meandor would fail, but he is in hiding. Inioch is loosed upon the earth again-risen from the dead, by Meandor's hand. But Meandor has retreated. Dark Elf holdings are falling to the onslaught of this new force of Inioch's, the Undead. And I am left alone to ponder the fate of this world. Do I side with the Dark Elves and Cult, or with the enticements of the risen Lord Inioch?
The Orcs and Goblins will follow me to the end. The Undead king promises me stature and an army unified under the cause of revenge. But I question the value of another king, when all others have failed me. Is it time that I stepped out from the shadow of these factions and took back the scepter of power which is thrust upon me? Do I choose the secure path of Undead rulers or the difficult path leading deep into the earth, to where the final faction awaits my leadership?
IN-GAME TEXT

Symon Scenario 1: Fairy Hill
is the first scenario in the tutorial of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders: Shadow Magic
. This and other scenarios in the tutorial are optional, but provide an overview of essential game mechanics, as well as a story introduction for Symon and Teryn and a backstory for the required sections of the campaign.
Story
The Peaceful lands around this hill are untouched by the events in the nearby Valley of Wonders. Guarded by fairies, this mystical hill is an ancient burial mound of the Halfling king, Smithan Proudfriend.
Symon, Julia has told me about you. I am Merlin. The apparition before you is named Teryn-a gifted, elusive spirit. Thanks to Teryn's talent, although I am suspended in shadow, my mind can escape this torturous prison. Like you, Symon, I have the gift of magic, and it has earned me many foes.
As an outcast, you must feel great anger and fear, but forgive me if I do not coddle you.  Phobius drives all people to madness. They allow their souls to weaken and decay, but you cannot afford the same mistake, no matter how justifiable.
See the light in the people who fear you. Learn compassion, as Julia has shown to you. She believes you have more than magic within you. If you heed my words, you shall learn great power, but without the guidance of your soul, you will forever be an outcast. This whole war is about the strength of souls.
—Merlin's intro
Outcome
Well done, my friend. By razing the Shadow Demon's city, you have proven to his mob that Vorsar is a liar. They know the Elves are no friend to Demons. Now that the sylvan creatures are organized, they will hold Norwood secure from attack by greedy men or demons. It pains me that you and your people must once again pay a terrible price to teach men to trust the good caretakers of this world. I fear it is your fate to suffer the tantrums of hungry, short-lived mortals.
In regards to your worries, I am not sure about the source of the Shadow Demons. Teryn says they are not from the world we call the Shadow World. Phobius justified banning magic in his empire, claiming he would starve the creatures, but they do not feed on magic. Phobius refuses to listen, so we must oppose him and hope that his people will not be fooled.
—Merlin's outro

Fire Sphere, Ep. 1
Scenario information
Story phase
Fire: initiation phase
Previous
Tutorial
(optional)
Next
Fire Sphere, Episode 2
Map attributes
Wizards
Merlin and Yaka
Map size
Large

Surface only
Victory condition
Defeat Yaka
Surface map
Fire Sphere, Episode 1
is the first scenario in the Fire Sphere section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders II: The Wizard's Throne
.
Story
The desire for vengeance burns within me. Did I choose this place or did Gabriel? I had family in this desert. I was born here. And here, I am reborn.
I lived here when times were pleasant, before demon cats slaughtered my people.  I have tried to rouse them to fight back, but they fear the cat people and their fire god, Yaka. I will dispel their superstition, and gain their trust.
—Merlin's opening monologue
Map features
Wizards
Merlin
- The player begins at the northwest corner with no cities
Yaka
(CPU Squire) - Yaka starts in the south east with the main city of Tanuar along with other cities
Notable structures
Camp Site
- South of the player's starting position; a stack of units will join for a fee
Magic Vault
- South of the player's starting position, in the desert area across the mountains
Magic Vault
- On an island on the east side of the map; provides the Healing Showers spell as a fixed reward
Ancient Ruin
- In the middle of the desert area south of the player's starting position
Camp Site
- At an oasis south of Yaka's main city; provides an item
Items
South of Cindra, near the boundary between the grassland and the desert
In a razed town northwest of Yaka's main city (this item will likely be claimed by Yaka before the player has a chance to do so)
Heroes
Belendor
(Human warrior) - Eligible to emerge; will offer to join Merlin as the scenario progresses
Jafsar
(Tigran priest) - Starting hero for Yaka
Walkthrough
This scenario is designed to have the player explore and expand by acquiring free units, which are labeled in the in-game interface as "refugees" when their stack is selected on the world map. Free units near Merlin's starting position include a halberdier, a knight, and a cavalry. Additionally, there is a camp directly south of Merlin's starting position, containing troops that will join for a small fee in gold. This starting set of acquirable units is sufficient to take Yaka's first city, Cindra, which is lightly guarded. Taking Cindra also provides a wizard tower for Merlin.
From this point, the player may expand to the following areas:
To the east of Merlin's starting position, there is a refugee crossbowman and a mine. There is also a swashbuckler and a transport ship southeast of the crossbowman. These refugees can be acquired before or after taking Cindra. Note that the swashbuckler has swimming and can explore the river area to the east.
Along the river, there is a human town called Kahiri that will freely join your forces. This town can be reached using the swashbuckler via the river, without having to cross through territory controlled by Yaka.
At the southeast area of the map, there is an Elven city that will freely join your forces. This area can be reached via the teleport to the southwest of Cindra. Upon approaching the town, an apparition will appear and offer the town to Merlin as a token of friendship to Humans, also explaining that she has little power outside of the Valley of Wonders. Gabriel will then identify the apparition as Julia, Queen of the Elven Court.
Yaka is only a squire-level opponent. However, he begins with three cities under his control and will typically capture at least two additional cities near his initial domain. Yaka's extensive starting position compared to the player's meagre starting position makes this a potentially difficult first scenario if the player does not expand quickly and aggressively or does not take advantage of the freely available units and cities, in which case the player can be overwhelmed by the sheer amount of units that Yaka can train. To explore efficiently, it is often beneficial to split units with swimming (such as swashbucklers) or high movement points (such as cavalry) from the main force to explore on their own.
Completing this scenario requires defeating Yaka in battle when he does not have any remaining cities with a wizard tower. Note that if Yaka is carrying items and is defeated in his last remaining city that has a wizard tower, the scenario will end before you are able to acquire the items in his inventory. One method to acquire such items is to use a "trap city." For example, there is another city (Icran) near Yaka's main city of Tanuar. If you capture Icran, build a wizard tower there, and allow Yaka to recapture Icran, then defeating Yaka at Tanuar will cause Yaka to teleport Icran while dropping all the items that he was carrying.
Before completing this scenario, it is also preferable to acquire the Healing Showers spell at the east side of the map, since the Fire sphere does not have any healing spells of its own.
Outcome
I established peace and now my people possess a good land. I also struck a deal with Karissa. Her Orcs can have the arid lands I took from Yaka. She was amazed that a wizard would give back any of his domain.  These wizards desperately seek lands by any means.  But why?
Artica is furious that I would favor Karissa, but how could I support Artica? She would encase this desert realm in ice and throw the world out of balance. Sadly, she may now be my permanent enemy.
—Merlin's closing monologue
Trivia
At the time of release, this scenario had a reputation for being difficult as a first proper scenario for the game. GameSpot wrote, in the context of the game's complexity and lack of adequate tutorials, that "one of Age of Wonders II's campaigns (the Fire Sphere campaign) proved to be too hard for most new players."
References

Fire Sphere, Episode 2
is the second scenario in the Fire Sphere section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders II: The Wizard's Throne
.
Story
I remember visiting a place near the mountains where rivers of ice flow downward towards the desert sands. Between mountain and desert, the melting ice has created fertile lands. Gabriel warned me of two wizards nearby who war over these precious green fields. If they remain at war, I can topple them both. The Humans will have a fertile homeland.
Once my people find safety, then I will discover why Gabriel's wizards rebel against him. First, I must attend to my people.
—Merlin's opening monologue
Map features
Wizards
Merlin
- The player begins at the west edge of the map with two pioneers and a token force.
Artica
(CPU Knight) - Artica is located in the Ivory Glaciers
in the north and controls the frostling city of Frostgate
Karissa
(CPU Knight) - Karissa controls the Orc city of Araksar in the southeast and will offer peace with Merlin when first met
Notable structures
Camp Site
- South of Merlin's starting position, in the southwest steppes
Ancient Ruin
- In the southwest steppes, to the southwest of Shira
Haunted Crypt
- Directly east of Shira, near the road
Dragon's Lair
- Near a lava area at the east side of the north section of the underground
Camp Site
- Near the first razed city reached by following the road; a pioneer and two units will join for a fee
Heroes
Shira
(Tigran rogue) - Independent-refugee hero located at the steppes to the southeast of Merlin's starting position. When met, Shira will state that she has fled to this land due to despising Yaka, and will offer to join at no cost
Khitan
(Frostling ranger) - Eligible to emerge (will likely join Artica)
Wazz
(Orc rogue) - Eligible to emerge (will likely join Karissa)
Jattah
(Goblin rogue) - Eligible to emerge (will likely join Karissa)
Walkthrough
This scenario serves as a tutorial for using pioneers. At the beginning, Merlin has no cities, but has two pioneers that can be used to build cities (starting at the outpost level) or repair razed cities. Upon reaching the hill just to the southeast, Gabriel will suggest building an outpost there, also noting that building close to water enables ships to be built. From the standpoint of optimality, a better choice for the pioneers would be further along the road to the southeast, which leads to a trio of razed cities that can be repaired. However, since this is a relatively easy scenario compared to the previous one, the choice on where to use the pioneers is not a particularly important one. If you build an outpost on the hill using one pioneer, you can still use the other to repair the city to the east.
Traveling in the southeast direction, you will also come across Shira, who will join along with two Tigran units. Shira will likely become your second hero, after acquiring Belendor in the previous scenario.
If you accept Karissa's peace offer at the beginning, you will typically be able to ally with her later on. The objective then becomes simply defeating Artica. If you do not ally with Karissa, then you must also defeat her as well.
Outcome
I established peace and now my people possess a good land. I also struck a deal with Karissa. Her Orcs can have the arid lands I took from Yaka. She was amazed that a wizard would give back any of his domain.  These wizards desperately seek lands by any means.  But why?
Artica is furious that I would favor Karissa, but how could I support Artica? She would encase this desert realm in ice and throw the world out of balance. Sadly, she may now be my permanent enemy.
—Merlin's closing monologue

Fire Sphere, Episode 3
is the optional third scenario in the Fire Sphere section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders II: The Wizard's Throne
.  As in the case of other optional third scenarios, this scenario does not need to be completed in order to advance the campaign. However, this scenario reveals additional story information, and provides an opportunity for the player to further level any acquired heroes.
Story
Yaka rouses his forces in his ancient home, the birthplace of the Azracs, intent on slaying all the humans. His Tigrans have gained great power from this Sea of Fire.
Karissa offered me command of an elite group of Orcs.  These savage creatures are well-suited to withstand the hellish heat of Yaka's volcanic heartland. I will make good use of them. Yaka's cruel dream must be stopped.
—Merlin's opening monologue
Map features
Wizards
Merlin
- The player begins at the southwest island with one city, Smokston
Yaka
(CPU Lord) - Yaka begins with multiple cities, including the main city of Infernus at the northeast corner of the map
Nekron
(CPU Lord) - Nekon begins with with multiple cities on the east side of the map, including the main city of Kalalak at the east edge
Notable structures
Magic Vault
- Northwest corner of the map, northwest of Yakala
Ancient Ruin
- Near the northewest corner of the map, at a position north of Yakala
Dragon's Lair
- Northeast part of the map, southeast across the lava from Yaka's main starting city
Items
The area to the northwest of the player's starting position has an item bag guarded by a glutton
The magic vault at the northwest corner has an item bag at the same position
Heroes
Jack
(Undead rogue) - Starting hero for Nekron
Walkthrough
This scenario requires defeating two opponents who are both at the relatively formidable CPU Lord level. The map has a relatively complex layout that includes multiple teleportation routes around the edges of the map, as well as an underground layer. Lava can be walked on by ground units enchanted by the Fire Halo spell, which can be used to reach the main cities of Yaka and Nekron on the far side of the map.
Outcome
The Sea of Fire is mine. Yaka has no more power in this land. I will take its more powerful magic for my people and then give these lands to Karissa and her Orcs. With her Orcs far away, Karissa can prosper without the temptation of my people upon her borders. My humans will be safe while I pursue Gabriel's agenda upon the mainland of the Blessed Continent.
—Merlin's closing monologue

Gabriel's Last Stand
is the first scenario in the Highmen route of the
campaign
in
Age of Wonders
, and the 8th scenario in the campaign overall if the Highmen route was chosen. The Highmen route is an option available in the
Keepers
version of the campaign under all preceding routes, and is also available in the
Cult of Storms
version of the campaign if the player previously assisted the Lizardmen.
Story
Main
Keepers
Cult of Storms
Select a campaign faction from the tabs above to view the corresponding text.
Born Again
A choice had to be made. One which would secure the future peace of this world. Let Julia remain forever with her Elves. She lives, locked in tradition. The Keepers may not understand my choice, but they will. I made mistakes. Too many mistakes. The Highmen care nothing of that, but welcome me with warm embraces. They offer me redemption from my poor choices and absolve me of guilt. Their power is beyond this realm, and penetrates my core. The voices of darkness are quelled in my heart, and I am free to see with the light the Highmen emanate.
Yet, the cost of my salvation is steep. My advocate with the Highmen's High Council is in peril. Without my help, Gabriel will perish. The Undead, seeking to destroy my alliance with the Highmen, trapped Gabriel's army near Blackwater Lake. They have driven him far from me. Without Gabriel's help I will be unable to communicate with the Highmen. It is their order of things, and I must respect order. I will go and do the things I am commanded by the Highmen, to prove my loyalty is beyond question.
About the Highmen
The Highmen appear to descend from heaven in times of crisis to aid Humans. They live in perfect harmony, in a society of equals, governed by a ruling body called the High Council. They keep to themselves, yet have high esteem for races which pursue good endeavors. They are mysterious and do not speak of their military might except in battle hymns that I have to confess seem exaggerated. They do not fear death, and viciously seek to obliterate undeath. Little else is known of this enigmatic people, which explains the distrust given them by other races.
IN-GAME TEXT (KEEPERS VERSION)
Turnabout
I am not stupid. War is about power. The powers now unleashed upon the world rival anything of the Keepers or Cult. I refuse to be caught on the losing side. The Undead are monsters -more appetite than mind. If I sided with them, I would end up in their bellies. While the cult hides in gloom, I seek the one force able to resist the Undead. For some reason, the Highmen give me peace of mind. I can think clearly, more so than I ever did in subservience to Meandor. Yet, I find much of the Highmen ways barely tolerable.
They talk incessantly of nobleness and unattainable virtues. The ruling body of the Highmen, known as the High Council, will have nothing to do with me, claiming I am unclean. A messenger has informed me that if I am to remain with them, I will need to rescue my liaison, a Highman named Gabriel, who will speak to them for me. Ironically, the force of Undead I unleashed at Blackwater Lake split his forces and Gabriel has been trapped, unable to break through to freedom. I will save him and he will do what I want out of gratitude.
About the Highmen
The Highmen employ a most impressive array of units in the battlefield and are optimal in combat against the Undead. They do not talk of their military prowess for good reason. What the enemy doesn't know gives the Highmen greater advantage. I have tried to ascertain further information but the citizens are strangely united in their convictions to keep such details secret. They claim their weapons are sacred and it is irreverent to discuss them. I must remember that if I ever rejoin the Cult. It is a wonderful excuse for hiding the nastiest surprises.
IN-GAME TEXT (CULT VERSION)

Walkthrough
The player begins at the center of the map, surrounded by hostile settlements on all sides. The Undead has a large number of cities, but fortunately few forces that pose an immediate threat in the beginning, allowing the player to expand in a desired direction. The Undead leader will typically be encountered at the southwest corner of the map.
An unusual feature of this map is that the player has an external income of 30 gold per turn. External income is commonly used to boost the strength of AI-controlled factions, but is applied to the player in this scenario.
Outcome
Main
Keepers
Cult of Storms
Select a campaign faction from the tabs above to view the corresponding text.
Deliverance
I am unworthy of praise, yet Gabriel persists. If only Julia could hear it. She and the Keepers think I have betrayed them, but I have not. I love them all the more, now that I am among the Highmen. I cannot help but feel the grace of these beings sharpening my own desire to be noble. Gabriel speaks of the noble path and his confidence is inspiring. Gabriel says that a great time of change comes, and that I should rejoice. When I fear, he chastises me gently, reminding me that fear is the food of demons.
IN-GAME TEXT (KEEPERS VERSION)
Ingratitude
Gabriel is slow to acknowledge my hand in his rescue. He mumbles something about the virtue of humility. He should thank me for cleaning up the mess I unleashed at Blackwater. He tells me little, except in lectures. He wields great power as a Highman, but his eyes turn downward as though he were a coward. When he does speak, it is always something nauseatingly positive, as though the war was a diversion, or not the most important thing that this world has ever faced. Still, they have afforded me the finest fighting force in the world.
IN-GAME TEXT (CULT VERSION)

Walkthrough
The Frostlings begin very close to the player, so close that their main city is reachable by a leader with at least 40 movement points, making it possible to defeat the Frostlings on the first turn of the scenario if your leader is capable of breaching walls and capturing the city alone. Defeating the Frostlings opens up the map to towards the Dark Elves and the Undead.
Although the story text mentions Durlag as the objective, completing this map will require defeating all other factions.

Gabriel is anxious to tell me more of the Highmen and I admit I find it all quite fascinating. I have nearly forgotten Julia in all this. Forced Charity

I do not covet the rewards that the Highmen will give them.

Story
Discipline
Will I allow my children to go astray? How can they forsake me so? After all that I have given them, they pin their hopes in Keeper lies and the feeble aid of Halflings and Dwarves! They would cash in their favored rank for immediate reward, but they err. Have they learned nothing? My Goblin children must first labor, then they will know freedom from bondage. The Goblin heretic, Gurkin, aided by the Keepers, will be put down, and my children will know the punishment of infidelity. The mountains will not shelter them from my nurture.

Walkthrough
The player starts off with very little, and must expand outward. Fortunately, the benefit of fighting against Goblin opponents is that race relations with Orcs are good, resulting in no unrest in Goblin cities that you capture.
Another consideration is that the there are major independent Human cities close to the player's starting position, including a size 3 city at the starting area and two size 4 cities across the water. Therefore, forging good relations with Humans (by upgrading, fortifying, and migrating Dwarf/Halfling cities to Humans) may be worthwhile.
Outcome
Homecoming
My children returned to me. Infants. They are impressionable. I have impressed the necessity of fidelity upon them. They will not stray again. And where are the deceivers who brought my children such anguish? Did the Keepers keep them from harm? As always they talk peace, but are helpless to back their pretty words with actions. Peace is a lie. The wild world teaches that only the strongest predators survive. All must fall prey to their appetites. I regret not my actions. My children are stronger now. Both Orc and Goblin are ready for the awaiting hunt.

Goblin Rush
Scenario information
Campaign
Keepers

Halflings
Next

or
Subterranean Path

150 (to next scenario)

3
Victory condition

Surface map
Goblin Rush
, also known as
Flowershire
, is the first scenario in the
Keepers version
of the
campaign
in
Age of Wonders
. It is the first scenario in the Halflings section of the campaign.
Story
Goblin Rush
The gathering Goblins invaded Flowershire, home of the Halflings. Not normally a fighting people, the Halflings are ironically our most loyal allies. They believe in the Keepers cause and see little value in gold, fighting instead for right and the chance to inspire heroic ballads. I am told there may be forces other than Halfling lurking near, seeking revenge against the Goblins. If I can find these renegades, surely they will help in my fight against the Cult. If the Halflings are to keep this haven, I must see that no Goblin remains in this serene vale.
About the Halflings
Halflings are peaceful beings, touched by the faerie-folk, filled with curious notions. They have survived for centuries on the mere fact that most races ignore them. They value gold only if it can be used for good. Halflings are inexpensive to hire, fighting for noble causes and the chance at making legends. Nimble and quick, they make capable Swordmen. Though physically weak, they Parry attacks naturally. With arms too short for bows, they are deadly with a sling and stones. Their smallest Hamlets can produce wall-crushing Battering Rams. Halflings also employ Ponyriders, more as scouts than cavalry.
IN-GAME TEXT
Map features
Starting positions and cities
Halflings
(player-controlled) - The player begins at the northwest corner of the map with no cities. However, there are four independent halfling cities nearby that will join for gold.
Goblins
(
CPU Squire
) - The opponent begins with four cities. The main Goblin city, where the Goblin leader begins, is a 3-hex city named Beslath located across the river at the southeast edge of the map.
Notable structures
Castle Ruin
(low item value) - Located in the southwest of the map
Monster Lair
(average item value) - East of the river, near the road running between the two 2-hex cities
Wizards Tower
(level 1 spell of any sphere except Death and Fire) - Near the south bridge
Heroes
CPU Leaders: Bunto (Goblins)
Walkthrough
At the start, it is advantageous to split your starting stack in order to simultaneously enlist the nearby independent Halfling troops and cities as quickly as possible. The two farms near the starting area should also be taken, since farms generate gold. After gaining the independent troops, cities, and farms, you will have a relatively large force and should begin fighting or advancing against the opponent's forces, especially since you will also a relatively large upkeep for the troops gathered.
After the first several turns, Goblin forces will likely appear along the two road respectively leading south and southeast from the starting position, with the south direction typically seeing larger enemy forces. These two directions correspond to the two bridges on the river. One strategy is to split your forces to hold one direction and advance in the other. In particularly, the route to the upper bridge (southeast of the starting position) can be controlled and blocked off from enemy forces simply by positioning a stack on the road between the hills, allowing you to advance in the south. Note that since Halflings and Goblins have poor relations by default, it will be necessary to stabilize captured Goblin cities, such as by migration to Halflings, maintaining a garrison, or razing the city.
Defeating the Goblin leader in battle completes the map. Prior to doing so, note that the map includes two lairs offering random
items
, as well as a wizards tower that may offer a useful spell. After completing this scenario, the player must choose between one of two routes, which will determine the next scenario that is played.
Outcome
The Flowershire is Saved!
The Halflings will now have sanctuary for their women and children, should battle grow fierce. The Halflings have proven fine allies. Yet, even as the last Goblin fell and cheers rang out, scouts brought news of a greater threat to halflingkind. The United Cities are imperiled. Meandor spares no expense to see the wee folk pay for open allegiance with the Keepers. As I write, we race to aid their island cities against thronging evil. I must decide whether to pursue rumors of a subterranean path under the mountains or brave the Northern Trade Route.
IN-GAME TEXT
Gallery
The Flowershire as depicted in-game and the starting position of this scenario
Unused map texture in the game files showing an early design of the map with only one bridge
Notes
"Goblin Rush" is the name of this scenario in the campaign map interface. However, the map file defines the map name as "Flowershire," which is the name that is used in the save file that is automatically generated upon completion of this scenario. The map file name is also used in the
Official Strategy Guide
, which refers to this scenario as "The Flowershire."
A sign at the northwest road reads "The Northern Trade Route," which refers to one of two possible paths to the United Cities, as explained in the outcome story text.

Hall of Heroes
is the third scenario in the Dwarves route in the
Keepers version
of the
campaign
in
Age of Wonders
,
and the 6th scenario in the campaign overall.
Story
Hall of Heroes
While exchanging ghost stories, the Dwarves told a tale that piques my interest. After King Inioch perished, the Dwarves decided to create the safe haven, Deepmir, but their greatest heroes disappeared before the great nation was founded, vanishing in a cave near here. Ill-fated attempts to rescue them only fuel endless ghost stories. Ever the Masters of dark foreboding, I suspect the Cult of Storms. Legends state the heroes will return, "In dire need." I intend to investigate this story for we have great need of help, and there is time before the Dwarves arrive in the Safelands.
IN-GAME TEXT
Map features
Starting positions and cities
Dwarves
(player-controlled) - The player begins at the southwest corner with the size 2 city Berdask.
Dark Elves
(
CPU Lord

Frostlings

Notable structures

(average item value) - In the northwest quadrant of the depths level
Heroes
The following heroes can be recruited at the Hall of Heroes by interacting with them on the map:
Bormac Orcbane
(Dwarf, level 11)

Other heroes that appear in this scenario:
Norshin War Priest
(Frostlings)
Vandir the Exile
(Dark Elves)
CPU Leaders: Hagar (Frostlings), Celarn (Dark Elves)
Walkthrough
The objective is to reach the Hall of Heroes located in the underground, which has a maze-like, two-layer layout similar in style to the earlier scenario
Earthquake
. Compared to Earthquake, the routes in Hall of Heroes are not nearly as complex, but the opponents are stronger (being at Lord and Knight levels) while the player's starting position is vulnerable to attack.
The player's starting position is vulnerable because the starting area does not have adequate resources to support a large army and there are three cave entrances nearby that the Dark Elves can attack from. The AI is not held back by the complexity of the underground map, and will expand rapidly if left unchecked.
Strategies
One strategy is to keep moving while letting the AI take your cities. Since capturing enemy cities is not required, you only need a single strong stack that can withstand any AI army and to use it to find the Hall of Heroes. If necessary, cities of hostile races can be looted for gold in order to prevent units from
deserting
due to lack of upkeep payment.
Another strategy is to defeat the Dark Elves as early as possible in order to avoid attacks from the underground. Head to the cave entrance directly east of the starting position (near the independent 1-hex Goblin city Borshein), and travel then east in the caverns level to find another downward entrance. From here, the Dark Elves' size 4 starting city (where their leader is typically found) is to the southeast, across a bridge over lava.
A similar strategy is to defeat the Frostlings on the surface as early as possible. The shortest route is to cross the river near Borshein (using, for example, the
Freeze Water
spell or
Dwarven Ballons
transferred from the previous map). It is also possible to reach the Frostlings through the caverns level by using one of two exits to the surface respectively located southwest and southeast of the size 4 Goblin city Hollowdeep in the caverns.
Reaching the Hall of Heroes
In order to reach the Hall of Heroes, you must locate a teleport that is at the center of the northern part of the caverns level. This section of the caverns is not directly connected to the southern section; instead, reaching the area requires traveling through either the depths or the surface.
From the depths level, there are two entrances from the central northern part of the depths level. These entrances that will lead to the central northern part of the caverns level where the teleport is located.
The northwest part this map contains a series of caverns by which all three levels can be accessed via cave entrances that are relatively close to each other. From the northwest part of either the surface level or the depths level, there are cave entrances that lead to the northwest part of the caverns level, which then leads to the central northern part of the caverns level where the teleport is located.
The teleport will provide a one-way trip to the Hall of Heroes area, where you can recruit three heroes. Unfortunately, unless campaign difficulty is set to easy (which doubles the transfer limit), it is impossible to carry all three heroes into the next scenario. The next scenario has a transfer limit of 675 at normal difficulty, which is not enough to accommodate a level 11 hero (312 transfer points) along with two level 7 heroes (212 transfer points each). Note that if you already have a second hero who has reached level 13 (the level cap for this map), that hero will require 362 transfer points. In practice, depending on what is needed for the next scenario, it might not be practical to transfer any of the three new heroes.
This map can also be completed by defeating both opposing factions. However, doing so will end the map early without the opportunity to recruit the heroes at the Hall of Heroes.
Outcome
Legend No More
The legend is no more. The awakened heroes are eager to assist Julia, and the Dwarves. I wish I had more time to pursue the other legends and superstitions, which echo throughout dwarven campfires, but now graver talk fills our ears. Letters, found among the Cult's holdings, reveal Stormlord Melenis orchestrated the collapse of Deepmir and used it to threaten the Frostlings into hostility against Keepers and Dwarves. And while we've dealt the Cult a blow, from what I have read, Melenis is organizing a massive strike against the Dwarves, before we have built up in the Safelands.
IN-GAME TEXT
Notes
According to the story text at the end of
Ashen Steppe
in the
Cult of Storms campaign
, Bormac was originally trapped by the Cult.
Bormac's return is the premise of
Facing a Legend
in the Cult campaign. In that scenario in the Cult campaign, the player is tasked with defeating Bormac. In the Keepers campaign, however, Bormac's fate is open-ended and the player has the option of carrying over Bormac into the next scenario. In the series' canon, Bormac survives the events of the campaign.

Symon Scenario 3: Heimburg Havens
is the third scenario in the optional tutorial section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders: Shadow Magic
.
Story
This small fishing community has little tolerance for strangers or 'eccentrics'. After Phobius claimed these lands as his own, shamans and mages fled the ensuing persecution. Their 'gift' turned against them.
You are ready to return to your homeland. Seek to bolster the people's confidence in you. You have learned of the Shadow demons' love of souls. Fear is their strength, but you have a greater power.
Like the demons, Phobius rules by intimidation, pointing out differences and establishing strict rule over magic. Only those he deems worthy are allowed to use magic. He claims we abuse magic from birth, while he will waste cities if it suits his image. Those that criticize him disappear by the hand of the brutal Vorsar, his first commander. I have given you strength enough to inspire your people to throw off their lies. Purge Heimburg of Phobius and his lackey Vorsar.
—Merlin's intro
Map features

Heroes

Walkthrough
This scenario includes a tutorial on alliances, including the use of the diplomacy interface. Julia serves as Symon's ally against Vorsar, and the map is set up so that Julia's allied forces will provide assistance against Vorsar's second and third cities.
Outcome
The void wavers. Phobius's defeat has affected these creatures as well. Interesting. I will have to ponder the strange connection between the Phobian Empire and these demons. Somehow the Shadow Demons benefit from the hateful human empire. You will need to maintain these lands. I trust you to hold them until my rebel wizards can strike at them elsewhere. I strongly believe this empire of fear will fracture, unable to fight on every front.
Beware the crippling powers of fear, hate and anger. I trust you to avoid such traps. Your courage has given me strength to endure my hellish torture. For that, I thank you. Julia was right. You  have strength of spirit well beyond your years. Farewell, Symon. I look forward to the day I call upon your aid again.
—Merlin's outro

PAGE: Horn of Kesh

Horn of Kesh
Scenario information
Story phase
Ke-nan
Next

Map size
Large
Map layers

Victory condition
Defeat Sahira
Surface map
Underground map
Shadow realm map
Ke-nan Scenario 1: Horn of Kesh
is the first scenario in Ke-nan's section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders: Shadow Magic
. Ke-nan's scenarios are optional and can be played at any time during the campaign, but they provide backstory for other parts of the campaign.
Story
The unforgiving Desert of Kesh can make life difficult, with oases few and far apart. Yet, the tribes of Nomads call it home and base their slave trade here, raiding the surrounding lands.
Ke-nan. It's Merlin. Sadly, while you journeyed to the Wizard's Council your father died. Sahira, your father's Shaman, has grown accustomed to your Royal Tent, and refuses to leave it.  She plots your demise, for she will do anything to keep her place among the Nomads. Seduced by the Shadow Demons, she promises to restore your people to an age of power unmatched even by your ancestors of the ancient Azrac Empire.
Sahira believes the demons will spare her people as they consume the world. With their aid, she has enslaved many of the surrounding peoples and is delivering them to the demons. Sadly, these races' hatred of the nomads is greater than ever and they don't care that you are not to blame for their losses.
—Merlin's intro
Map features
Wizards
Ke-nan (player) - The player begins at the northeast of the map
Sahira (CPU Knight) - Sahira begins with cities across the map, with her main city located at the south section
Marinus (CPU Squire) - Marinus begins with a small section in the northeast along the coast
Karissa (CPU Squire) - Karissa begins with three cities in the underground
Item lairs
Shipwreck
(random item) - South of the player's starting position
Heroes
Ashela (Nomad Warrior) - Will offer to join upon Ke-nan's arrival at the first city
Taballu (Nomad Rogue) - Can be recruited at the arena to the southeast of the player's starting position
Khaan (Nomad Ranger) - Hero for Sahira
Pitface (Nomad Warrior) - Hero for Sahira, located in the pit at the southeast section of the map
Walkthrough
Upon arriving at the first city and recruiting Ashela, the game will provide a tutorial on the "move city" feature unique to the Nomads and will suggest relocation of the initial city to the east in order to flee from Karissa's orcs. Upon relocating the city, the map opens up to exploration. The map includes the following optional interactions:
South of your starting city's new location is an arena where the hero Taballu can be recruited.
Many pit lords can be encountered, along with slaves that can join your forces.
If you successfully raid the dungeon marked by the sign "Halfling Storage" just north of the center of the map, Marinus will offer to ally with you. Since Marinus is a water wizard, having him as an ally provides the benefit of being able to acquire his spells through the diplomacy interface.
Marinus is isolated from the rest of the map by invisible AI-blocking barriers that prevent him from sending units into the rest of the map. These barriers are cleared when visited by a player-controlled unit. Therefore, to clear these barriers so that Marinus can potentially offer military assistance against Sahira, you must send a unit to his area through the area with a sanctuary, and then fully cross the bridge to his domain.
Karissa will offer to ally with you if you defeat Pitface, a hero that is located in the pit at the southeast of the surface map (as discussed below). Karissa is blocked off from the rest of the map by AI-blocking barriers. These barriers can be cleared by sending a unit to the Furnace just outside of the cave leading to her area.
The main objective is to defeat Sahira, whose main city is at the south section of this map. After you have captured this city, Sahira will unexpectedly relocate to the shadow realm. In order to pursue and defeat her in the shadow realm, you must use the teleport at the east of the central region of the map, located in a lava lake. This teleport exits at the pit at the southeast of the map, where Sahira's hero Pitface is encountered. This area, which has a number of recruitable independent units, eventually leads to another teleport, which accesses the shadow realm.
Once inside the shadow realm, a scripted event will spawn several stacks of Shadow Demon units for Sahira around her shadow realm city. Defeating Sahira will complete the scenario.
It is possible to break the above sequence by stepping into teleport at the lava lake before capturing Sahira's main city on the surface. In this case, if you capture the city in the shadow realm before Sahira retreats from the surface, that city in the shadow realm will be automatically be flagged to Sahira when she does retreat. For additional information on the mechanics of breaking the intended sequence in this manner, please see the "notes" section below.
Outcome
Rest now, Ke-nan. Mourn your Father's passing as is your right and custom. The Nomads will bow to the funeral pyre, and swallow the sparks that fly from the blaze, and your Father will rest with honor in the skies.
Though it brings little comfort, let me assure you that Sahira has not escaped in exile. She was snatched away by the Shadow Demons, only to learn what comes of one who bargains with these hungry creatures. She is in their debt now. In the end, your victory will consign her to the same grim fate that she forced upon her slaves.
—Merlin's outro
Notes
Normally, the shadow realm city is independent city until Sahira is defeated on the surface. However, if you enter the shadow realm prematurely, the city will also be given to Sahira prematurely. This triggerable event is independent of the one that flags the city for Sahira when she retreats from the surface, which will also be triggered if you capture the shadow realm city and then defeat her on the surface.
Once you've entered the teleport at the lava lake, there is no teleport path back to the main part of the surface. Return is possible only by building a teleportation gate in the city in the shadow realm, flying/floating over the mountains (e.g., by use of the Wind Walking spell), or using the Recall Hero spell.
If you are currently holding the shadow realm city when Sahira retreats from the surface, any units you have inside the city will be expelled when the city is flagged to Sahira. However, those units can be used to immediately recapture the city, since Sahira will not spawn in the city until the next turn.

Inioch's Touch
is the 3rd scenario in the Dark Elves route of the
Cult of Storms version
of the campaign in
Age of Wonders
, and the 10th scenario in the campaign overall if this route was chosen.
Story
Night Fevers
Since Inioch's return, Meandor has been in a state of torment. His nights are fitful and his days filled with visions only he can see. Gossip creates heretics claiming he is mad. My servants speak of phantoms within his shadow, clinging to him as his own breath. Inioch has sought to send Undead forces to capture Meandor, but they have been repelled. Now, Meandor's torment stops, and Inioch focuses on new targets. With his mind freed from demons, Meandor has ceased to hope for his father. Likewise, Inioch's will is free to pursue me and my Dark Elves.
Inioch's motives are pure, but he's dead. He sees life as incomplete. Blood ties him to Meandor and all Elves. Seeing them as corrupt, Inioch desires to purify all Elves in undeath. All this amuses me. Even now, a mass of Doom Priests approach to convert us either in life or death. Inioch is nearly right. Surface Elves are corrupt. Death improves them. More so, Highmen follow the Undead, desiring to convert us to their sanctimonious ways. But Dark Elves are not easily swayed, and we know the Highmen to be traitors to justice by aiding the despicable Human race.
IN-GAME TEXT
Map features
Starting positions and cities
Dark Elves
(player-controlled) - The player begins with two ships and no cities at the south part of the map.
Highmen
(CPU Lord) - The Highmen begin with two cities, the size 4 city Apocatastasis and the size 3 city Nothery, at the west section of the map.
Undead
(CPU Lord) - The Undead begin with two cities, the size 4 city Garzaer and the size 3 city Makak, at the east section of the map. The Undead and Highmen are are war with one another. Garzaer is protected by a static poison cloud.
Notable structures

Altar of Life
- In the Highmen section of the map

- In the Undead section of the map
Altar of Fire
- In the Undead section of the map
Heroes

(Dark Elf hero)

(Highmen)

(Undead)

Walkthrough
This map is one of the smallest in the whole campaign in terms of flat surface ground. The Highmen and Undead occupy nearly symmetric positions, with neutral Dark Elf cities in the middle just north of the neutral Human city at the shoreline. Since the Highmen and Undead are close by, capturing those Dark Elf cities early on is desirable.
Outcome
Held True
After countless onslaughts, we have prevailed. Only the purest Elves could accomplish such a feat. Through countless Lizardmen, Azracs, Frostlings, Elves, Undead and Highmen, we stand firm and determined. Yet, where are the others of the Cult? Gone. All shrink from the battle. My camp echoes of reports. Stormlords battle with every race upon the land, but not one has prevailed as I have. Many have been forced to surrender, and I am left alone--the only Stormlord capable of helping Meandor. Did I not foresee this? Their incompetence leads them to defeat, while I remain.
IN-GAME TEXT
