Southern Marsh
is the first scenario in the Lizardmen route of the
campaign
in
Age of Wonders
, and the 4th scenario in the campaign overall if the Lizardmen route was chosen. The Lizardmen route is an option available in both the
Keepers
and
Cult of Storms
versions of the campaign.
Story
Main
Keepers
Cult of Storms
Select a campaign faction from the tabs above to view the corresponding text.
Misconceptions
Julia is wrong. She will see it when I bring these Lizardmen to her in the Valley of Storms. Already I have learned more of the lizards and their forces than what is known among the Keepers. They only ask for a few tracts of land for their loyalty. Further, I see that we have a common enemy. The Frostlings threaten to freeze the lizards. Frostlings cannot be trusted, and must be driven out of the northern swamps. Despite tireless efforts to reason with the frozen creatures, the cold hearts refuse to give the lizards leave their rightful wetlands.
About the Lizardmen
Lizardmen live in a primal realm where lines of razor teeth devour the weak. As a result, they are often mistaken for carnivorous, evil brutes. Sadly, the Keepers share many of these falacies and perpetuate distorted stories to the more gullible races, such as the Halflings. Truthfully, though, Lizardmen must exhibit feral bias to survive, and their nature can be altered by shrewd diplomacy. As a race, they are closely bound to animal instinct and employ other animals to accomplish their more menial tasks. They are efficient and clever, capable of much good if given the opportunity.
IN-GAME TEXT (KEEPERS VERSION)
Pact of Convenience
Meandor is displeased with my choice, but it is time to find allies more worthy of the Cult of Storms. These lizards are far more clever than the brutish Orcs. Already they tire me with worthy demands, requiring I take back lands rightfully theirs. But they cannot fool me with their chameleon minds, I am kin to these devious reptiles. I'll let them use me for a time, then I will use them. I will grant their request, then they will grant mine. But for now I go to defeat Frostlings, intent upon freezing lizard holdings in solid ice.
About the Lizardmen
Lizardmen are aquatic by nature, covering marshlands and coastlines with their strange dwellings. Of all races, the lizards are most closely tied to the animal world. Caring little for good or evil, they favor ideals that promote their prosperity. Their weaponry is crude, yet efficient. They harness other wildlife to aid their civilization; such as the giant turtle, which they use as a beast of labor and for hauling weapons of war. Their bodies are equally suited for life on land or in the water, so they often control the most exotic and fertile lands.
IN-GAME TEXT (CULT VERSION)

Walkthrough
One advantage of Lizardmen is that almost all of their units have the swimming ability, which enables them to travel over water. This benefit is showcased on this map, which has two cities on islands in the middle of the lake northeast of the player's starting position. Both cities can be easily taken by Lizard units.
Your leader will most likely not have swimming (unless customized at the started of the campaign). However, the effect of swimming can be replicated by the
Water Walking
and
Wind Walking
spells, which can be useful in this part of the campaign.
The map itself is relatively straightforward in terms of layout and objectives. There is only one opponent, the Frostlings in the north, to defeat.

Keepers

Soured Success
The lizards have legitimately repossessed the land, which unjustly stolen from them. I had hoped our victory would brighten my brethren of the Keepers, but now they complain that the Frostlings have doubled their aggression against the Dwarves, blaming me for their inability to keep them at bay. What am I supposed to do? Should I turn my back while the Frostlings rob the lizards of their homeland? What makes the Dwarves more deserving of our aid? The lizards need me, but the prejudicial Keepers yield to me nothing but criticism.

Promise Kept

Now that I am freed from Meandor's shadow, I begin to wonder. Here in the swamp, where things with large snapping teeth devour things with smaller snapping teeth, I am beginning to see life according to the true order of things. These lizards desire a competent leader, one willing to guarantee them luxuries. They desire a leader like me.

Subterranean Path
is one of two possible choices for second scenario in the
Cult of Storms version
of the
campaign
in
Age of Wonders
. This scenario is played if the player chose to reach Lunaris via the subterranean route after completing
Goblin Rush
. The alternative scenario, if the player chose the trade route instead, is
The Northern Trade Route
.
The
Keepers campaign
also has a
corresponding version
of this scenario under the same name and with mostly the same map layout.
Story
Subterranean Path
A runaway slave, a Goblin once the property of an Orc warlord, fled from an underground passage infested with Dwarves.  In a show of magnanimous mercy, I have not to executed the Goblin fugitive. We'll all have plenty of new slaves, once the Halflings fall. The Orcs fight for control of the caves, and while I am tempted to aid them, the utmost goal is the city just through the caves called Lunaris.  It must fall within 20 days or the Cult's plans to take the United Cities will fall and the Keepers will win this war before it starts.
IN-GAME TEXT
Map features
Starting positions and cities
Halflings
(player-controlled) - The player begins at the northwest corner of the surface level with no cities, and must travel down the cave entrance to the caverns level in order to reach the destination.
Orcs
(
CPU Squire
) - The Orcs begin as allies with one city, Litiac in the southeast part of the caverns level.
Dwarves
(CPU Squire) - The Dwarves begin as opponents and hold one city, Dolsmar, near the center of the caverns level.
Notable structures
Monster Lair
(fixed loot:
Enchanted Pike
) - At the west side of the caverns level, northwest of the cave entrance after entering the cave.
Heroes
CPU Leaders: Gorbat (Orcs), Hallion (Dwarves)
Walkthrough
Compared to the alternative option of the Northern Trade Route, the main benefit of this map is that the monster lair at the west side of caverns guarantees an Enchanted Pike, which is one of the only items that have the valuable
First Strike
ability. The drawback, however, is that the hero given in the alternate map is missed, and a second hero will not be given until after the completion of the next scenario.
This scenario must be completed within 20 turns or else the game will trigger a loss. The objective is to arrive at the independent Halfling city of Lunaris, which is located on the east edge of the surface level. However, the only way to reach Lunaris is to travel down to the caverns level, and find an exit cave at the east side of the caverns. Reaching this exit cave requires traversing through Orc territory by staying near the south, southwest, and east edges of the caverns. However, before heading in this direction, you may wish to raid the monster lair on the west side of the caverns to obtain the Enchanted Pike.
Due to the time limit, conquering cities, unless incidental to exploration towards the destination, would likely be detrimental to completing this scenario in time.
In addition to the proper exit at the east, the caverns also contain a northwest exit that leads to an area on the surface level. This exit and corresponding surface area are not relevant to the objective, and and going there will only waste the limited amount of turns available. This exit and surface area are instead featured as part of the player's starting position in the Keepers version of this scenario.
Note that defeating the Dwarf leader alone will not grant victory in this scenario, because allied victory is not enabled. However, defeating both the Orcs and the Dwarves is available as an alternate victory condition. While the Orcs begin as allies, they may cancel the alliance and declare war if the Dwarves defeated, contrary to the actual story of the campaign. Being at war with the Orcs has no effect on the story of the campaign.
Outcome
A Simple Win
I can understand why my worshipers might flee the Orc chieftains. I can see that if the Orcs are to be valuable in this conflict, they will need my tutelage in battle. It nauseates me that the Orcs, with their formidable troops, could be intimidated by these Dwarven runts who dig in the dirt. Such incompetence! Is it any wonder that we have hidden in shadows for centuries? Destiny prods me righteously onward, justice requires I purge this corrupt world, and as Lunaris, all so-called fair races will fall, one by one before my might.
IN-GAME TEXT
Notes
Unlike the Keepers version of this scenario, the southeast area on the surface (which is the starting position for the Cult version) does not include the independent city Eudorn. This city is instead replaced by a mine.
It is possible to reach Lunaris by crossing the mountains on the surface of the map if you have
mountaineering
and/or
flying
units and are able to defeat one of the
Red Dragons
guarding the mountains.

Story
Subterranean Path
My Halfling advisers talk of a subterranean path through the mountains. Once the strict domain of Dwarves, the caverns echo with the sound of battle. Orc and Dwarven forces clash. Despite the dangers, that path -directly east- appears the fastest way to Lunaris and my little friends assure me the Dwarves are friendly, especially toward those who battle the Orcs. Map features
Starting positions and cities

CPU Squire

Walkthrough
Compared to the alternative option of the Northern Trade Route, the main benefit of this map is that the monster lair at the west side of caverns guarantees an Enchanted Pike, which is one of the only items that have the valuable
First Strike
ability. The drawback, however, is that the hero given in the alternate map is missed, and a second hero will not be given until after the completion of the next scenario.
This scenario must be completed within 20 turns or else the game will trigger a loss. The objective is to arrive at the independent Halfling city of Lunaris, which is located on the east edge of the surface level. However, the only way to reach Lunaris is to travel down to the caverns level, and find an exit cave at the east side of the caverns. Reaching this exit cave requires traversing through Orc territory.
Assuming that the Enchanted Pike is desired, the optimal path in the caverns is to travel along the east wall to acquire the item, and then travel southeast, east, and through the Orc territory to reach the exit. Due to the turn limit, there is generally no time to develop cities. Similarly, conquering cities, unless incidental to exploration towards the destination, would also likely be detrimental to completing this scenario in time.
The southwest exit from the caverns, which leads to an area on the southwest of the surface level with an independent city, has no purpose in this map and going there will only waste the limited amount of turns available. This exit and surface area are instead featured as part of the player's starting position in the Cult of Storms version of this scenario.
Note that defeating the Orc leader alone will not grant victory in this scenario, because allied victory is not enabled. However, defeating both the Orcs and the Dwarves is available as an alternate victory condition. While the Dwarves begin as allies, they may cancel the alliance and declare war if the Orcs defeated, contrary to the story of the campaign. Being at war with the Dwarves has no effect on the story of the campaign.
Outcome
Smoke on the Horizon
The Dwarves are fine warriors, fiercer than I'd remembered. I think the feeling was mutual, as Keeper forces revealed an ability to fight. The look of surprise on the face of their grizzled battle-captain shall keep me bemused for years. I will have to consider these Dwarven folk carefully, when the opportunity comes to recruit stronger allies. Our arrival in Lunaris energized the weary Halfling forces here. I have never seen people as euphoric as these are at our arrival. Their energetic spirit gives me hope in the face of foreboding afflictions.

O'neron Scenario 3: Sunbirth Mountains
is the third scenario in O'neron's section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders: Shadow Magic
.
Story
The eastern border to the Empire, and civilization. Few explorers have ventured beyond these mountains, and none have returned. It is said there is a great magical energy in the very rocks of these dark mountains.
Six elements of creation... Fire, Water, Earth, Air, Life and Death.  Each fuels the rift. O'neron, come. Join the conflux. Searing pain... Six elements form the world anew... Make the traitors pay! Destroy each. Destroy. They destroyed my Master Gabriel. They will destroy us all.
O'neron? Can you hear it? The All-Devourer knows! He knows your mission.  He has stopped fighting me for a moment. You are close to where I am. He readies a terrible force against you. I can only watch. Remember Freedom. Trust. Peel back this destruction.
—Merlin's intro
Map features
Wizards
O'neron
(Player) - O'neron begins at the southeast with no city.
Merlin
(CPU Squire) - Merlin is trapped in the shadow realm. He has no forces on the map and is only involved in scripted interactions.
Mab
(CPU King) - Mab begins at the southwest section of the underground
Tempest
(CPU King) - Tempest will spawn at the northeast section of the surface
Nekron
(CPU King) - Nekron will spawn at the south section of the surface
Nimue
(CPU King) - Nimue will spawn at the southeast section of the surface
Serena
(CPU King) - Serena will spawn at the north section of the surface. The city in which she spawns is hidden within the forest at the north edge of the map.
Yaka
(CPU King) - Yaka will spawn at the northwest section of the surface.
Item lairs
Shipwreck - Northwest section of the surface
Rainbow's End - North edge of the southeast section of the surface
2x Haunted Crypt - South section of the surface
Shipwreck - In the east side of the underground, just south of the air node and near the water node
2x Shipwreck - Southeast area of the underground
Magic vault
In the east side of the underground, just south of the air node and near the water node
Heroes
No new heroes appear on this map
Walkthrough
The premise of this scenario is that the six traitor wizards who were banished following the
campaign
of
The Wizard's Throne
are seeking to return to the world. The traitors have allied with the shadow demons to destroy the world
or for their own benefits.
West from the starting position is a ring of six teleports. Reaching the teleports will prompt Merlin to provide O'neron with the objective: destroy the 18 elemental nodes on the map to free Merlin from the shadow realm. Merlin explains that the traitor wizards' powers are linked to the nodes, and that breaking the nodes will break the wizards and set him free. Each element of fire, water, earth, air, life, and death has a node on each of the three level of the map. That is, there are 6 nodes on the surface, 6 in the underground, and 6 in the shadow realm, for a total of 18 nodes that must be destroyed.
Mab is already present on the map at the start of the scenario, while the other five wizards will spawn when one their corresponding elemental nodes in the underground is visited. For this reason, exploring too quickly early on may result in a situation in which you are faced with fighting multiple King-level opponents at once. This can be avoided by limiting or controlling your expansion. When all three nodes for a particular element have been razed, the corresponding wizard is automatically defeated.
At the ring of teleports, there are three possible paths forward:
The northwest teleport leads to the northwest part of the underground and generally provides the easiest path. From the teleport's destination, independent cities can be found nearby to the south and southeast. Progressing from the teleport's destination requires stepping on a fire node, which will cause Yaka to spawn.
The northeast teleport leads to the northeast part of the underground. From here, an independent city can be found nearby to the west, while additional cities are found far to the south. Progressing from teleport's destination requires stepping on an air node, which will cause Tempest to spawn. Traveling south to the additional cities requires stepping on an water node, which will cause Nimue to spawn.
A third option is to proceed northeast on the surface, which leads to encounters with two stacks of Basilisks. Progressing further reveals a cave entrance that leads to  the part of the underground controlled by Mab.
Outcome
The Invasion failed... The All-Devourer flees. I am mired in the anguish of every soul drawn into captivity by these demons. Chained by vices and tied to fear, they are flooded with hopelessness, but your victory has dispelled that intoxicating brew.
The rift seals, but I am still here in the void. There are many... Drifting... Though she knows the way, Teryn cannot free me. Only true Wizards can face the All-Devourer, and liberate these captive souls.
—Merlin's outro

Final Scenario: The Hive
is the final scenario in the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders: Shadow Magic

Story
A Well of Souls --The center of the Hive mind is a great prison, where souls damned by the Shadow Demons are shackled, packaged and processed for absorption into the Hive.
I-I found him.  Can it be?  One... among billions of spirits.  He strengthens me, as he once did. My old Master, Gabriel. I found his soul! The traitors exiled my friend to the Void-where the Shadow Demons slept. The All-Devourer awoke. They cannot hide their mind from me. They will close the rift and wait, as they always do. It is their instinct. They shall feed on sparks from their captive souls, while Men forget, Elves dwindle, and Magic is forsaken. Then they will return.
They used me to open the rift. I will hold it. Gabriel gives me strength. Hurry to the All-Devourer's heart. It may be certain doom, but it is all that we can do.
—Merlin's intro
Map features
Wizards

(player) - Merlin begins in the shadow realm near a shadow portal that leads to the west section of the underground

Meandor
(CPU squire) - Meandor begins in the southeast section of the surface
Ke-nan
(CPU squire) - Ke-nan begins at the southwest section of the surface

(CPU squire) - Symon begins at the northeast section of the surface
O'neron
(CPU squire) - O'neron begins at the north section of the surface
All-Devourer
(CPU King) - The All-Devourer holds multiple cities in the center of the shadow realm
Walkthrough
All previous campaign protagonists will appear as allies in this scenario. However, this scenario is independent of the previous scenarios, and does not utilize any carryover. The setup is six against one, but the All-Devourer is significantly more powerful than Merlin's allies combined. The All-Devourer has the benefit of a large amount of cities and resources in the underground and shadow realm, as well as scripted attack waves.
Upon stepping through the portal and arriving at the first city in the west section of the underground, Julia will give that city (Holluindom) to Merlin, while Meandor will also give a Draconian city (whose name is random) at the southeast section of the underground. Near Holluindom, the Human hero Paxanaria will join for free. Shortly after, the All-Devourer will begin attacking using scripted waves.
The first three waves consist of large numbers of Shadow Demon Lords and are expected to wipe out Ke-Nan, Symon, and Meandor, in that order, unless a specific strategy is used to keep them alive. The fourth wave is directed at O'neron, but is a weak wave that is expected to be defeated by O'neron. The scripted attack waves are as follows:
Day 10: First Wave
- A large force of Shadow Demon Lords will attack Ke-Nan's area. When this wave attacks, Meandor will grant Merlin a force of 1 Succubus and 3 Executioners with the intention of providing assistance to Ke-Nan.
Day 13: Second Wave
- A large force of Shadow Demon Lords will attack Symon's area. When this wave attacks, O'neron will grant Merlin a force of 1 1 Astral Sprite, 2 Giant Warriors, and 4 Lightning Catchers to assist Symon.
Day 22: Third Wave
- A large force of of Shadow Demon Lords will attack Meandor's area. During this wave, a single Lord will also appear in an area that can access the cave to Merlin's Draconian city. This Lord will usually reach and attack that city eventually.
Day 33: Fourth Wave
- The fourth wave, which is a nominal force of 1 Skimmer and 2 Stag Mounts, will attack O'neron. This wave is intended to be defeated by O'neron.
Five Wave
- The final scripted attack is a nominal force of 2 Skimmers. This wave is directed against Julia and is triggered only when the player approaches the sword location. There is no turn counter that triggers this wave.
The first three waves will despawn when the target wizards and their cities have been destroyed. Although this scenario sets up Ke-Nan, Symon, and Meandor to be defeated by the scripted attacks, Julia and O'neron are safe unless the player breaks the invisible barriers that restrict AI movement to their areas (see below for a full description of the key barriers).
During this scenario, the All-Devourer will attack Merlin's positions through one-way teleports that lead from the shadow realm to the Underground. The destinations of the one-way teleports have the appearance of pits. The three main pits in the underground layer are as follows:
The first pit is north of Holluindom.
The second pit is at the south edge of the west section of the underground, southwest of an independent Orc city. This pit will be a source of attacks from the All-Devourer if the player expands into the area past the Dwarven Mole southeast of Holluindom.
The third pit is in the south section of the underground, and will be a source of attacks from the All-Devourer if the player expands into the southwest of the Draconian city given by Meandor.
On day 18, Julia will inform Merlin that the only way to reach the shadow realm is to acquire a sword on the surface. This sword, named Donorian, is located at an area southeast of Julia's area that will be revealed during the course of the scenario. Acquiring this sword disables the force field blocking access to the shadow portals near O'neron's area. Access to these portals enables the player to reach the center of the shadow realm to capture the All-Devourer's cities. The shadow realm also contains a ring of enslaved cities that the player can freely acquire.
Therefore, the general objective of this scenario is to fend off the All-Devourer's attacks on the underground, while building enough forces to acquire the sword and eventually defeat the All-Devourer in the shadow realm. Specific strategies for accomplishing this goal are discussed below.
Specific strategies
Keeping allies alive
Although this scenario sets up Ke-Nan, Symon, and Meandor to be defeated, it is possible to keep them alive by placing a flying unit in their main cities. This method is typically performed by summoning Zephyr Birds on the hexes of the allied wizards' main city. As long as a single flying unit is placed on a city hex, that city cannot be taken by Shadow Demon Lords because Lords lack the ability to attack flying units. The Lords will not initiate combat if the opposing side has a flying unit.
This strategy requires either acquiring the Zephyr Bird spell or producing flyers from the Draconian city. The Zephyr Bird spell can be acquired either as a starting spell, through research, or from an ally via diplomacy. In practice, unless Merlin is customized at the start to specialize or focus on Air, successful acquisition of this spell is subject to a degree of randomness. Alternatively, it is also possible to keep allies alive by giving a city with a wizard's tower to them via the diplomacy interface.
Keeping Ke-Nan, Symon, and Meandor alive will not yield any substantial military benefit from them, because their territory is isolated from the shadow portals near O'neron, and their forces are weak compared to the All-Devourer's. However, by keeping the allies alive, it is possible to acquire their researched spells through diplomacy.
Acquiring the Tigran and Archon cities, and an Elven pioneer
There are two independent cities that can be acquired using the reinforce stacks given by Meandor and O'neron respectively for the first and second waves.
With the stack given by Meandor, the Tigran city can reached by traveling slightly west, and then north past the magic relay. Then, travel past the dungeon to reach a cave entrance to the underground with the Tigran city. This city can be conquered using the stack of units.
With units given by O'neron, separate the Astral Sprite from the rest of the stack and have it travel southeast into the water, to find a cave entrance on the lake. This cave entrance leads to an area of the underground, where an Archon will freely join.
Additionally, if the player places a unit near Julia's northwest city on the surface, she will give the player a pioneer that can be used to build a city on the surface. Without expanding through the barrier tiles discussed below, this area can be reached using summons.
Controlled expansion
While many campaign scenarios in the series reward early expansion, this particular scenario has the opposite design. This scenario relies heavy on invisible barriers (known as
AI Block
tiles in the map editor) that prevent CPU units from entering certain areas. These barriers are disabled when a human-controlled stack moves onto the tile, thus enabling that tile to be traveled through by the CPU. Therefore, aggressive expansion early on will remove these barriers, potentially creating paths by which the All-Devourer will attack. Conversely, not expanding into these tiles will preserve the invisible barriers, limiting the paths by which the All-Devourer can attack.
The most important barriers are as follows:
Southeast of Holluindom, there is a barrier around the Dwarven Mole that belongs to Julia. If you move a unit past the Mole, the All-Devourer will attack via the bone pit south of this area, thereby resulting in a two-front situation at Holluindom. If you do not move any unit past the Mole, the All-Devourer will not attack from this direction.
Southwest of the Draconian city given by Meandor, the independent goblin forces at the watch tower is on top of a barrier tile. If you take this watch tower, then the All-Devourer will be able to attack the Draconian city through the pit to the northwest of the watch tower.
From the Draconian given by Meandor, if you travel north and exit the cave entrance, there is a line of barrier tiles just outside of the cave entrance. If you move through these tiles, then the large stacks of Lords on the surface will be able to enter the cave.
North of Holluindom, there is a line of barrier tiles past the gold mine and just before the watch tower a few tiles to the northeast. Acquiring the gold mine itself does not disrupt this line. If you move through this line, the All-Devourer's forces teleported to the nearby pit will be able to enter Julia's area. A workaround to accessing Julia's territory without breaking this line is to use summons.
Avoiding breaking the first two barriers described above will enable to player to only have to defend Holluindom from the pit to the north, which simplifies the defensive strategy. Note that if desired, teleportation gates can be constructed in the player's cities to enable troop movement across the map without having to step through those barriers when ready.
Outcome
The All-Devourer is vanquished. His Demons retreat beyond the void where they held me. Billions of captive souls fly free and pass on to their final destination One of them lingers, it is my Master Gabriel.
Our meeting is brief. The Demons know this world now and that it is tainted by greed. Perhaps someday they will return, but for now they are on the run. O'neron and Teryn prepare with Gabriel to depart for distant worlds, looking for any trace of the Shadow Demons.
Julia, Meandor, Ke-nan and even young Symon will now return to help their people. Alliances, Prosperity, Security all traded for obedience. I confess I am skeptical. All I see is Phobius-his madness.
Bad leaders, good leaders: the differences are too subtle for me. Let others meddle with kings and knights. I want no more of it-just a quiet place. Let me fade from this world with the old magic.
Yes, that is my wish, let Merlin be forgotten from this coming Age of Men.
—Merlin's outro
Notes
The map file for this scenario has an unused internal map name of "Into the Void."

Story
Main
Keepers
Cult of Storms
Select a campaign faction from the tabs above to view the corresponding text.
Old Schools
When Inioch reigned, all wizards began their training on the Isle of Burbatak. Now Inioch desires the school and it's secrets returned to him. For more than a century since the fall of the Valley of Wonders, the vast island has known no single ruler. Many factions have come, trying to lay claim to the secrets entombed within the depths of the place, but none have conquered its twisted shorelines. With Inioch's power, I will reclaim the isle, returning Burbatak and the power it embodies to its rightful owner.

Isle of Burbatak
Inioch has chosen his next target, which like unto the first, is a source of great power. Even before Inioch reigned in life, the Elves gathered upon the Isle of Burbatak to learn mystic arts. All the greatest wizards were chosen and trained on the Isle. Since Inioch's fall the Isle has been under dispute by nearly every race, each hoping to exploit the island's secrets, but only a true pupil of the island's Master can claim it. Such a pupil would be a follower of Inioch, and so I shall reclaim the island for my Lord.

(CPU Lord) - The Lizardmen are the only AI faction without a city on the isle. Instead, they begin with a single city on the west rim of the lake, the size 4 city Marche. The Lizardmen are at war with all other factions, except the Frostlings, who are neutral.

Walkthrough
This is a multi-sided explore and expand scenario in which all factions have a well-defined starting positions on the map. The access paths on this map are also well defined. Each of the four AI factions with holdings on the center isle have a teleport from their respective position on the rim. A potentially unexpected inconvenience is that there is also a fifth faction, the Lizardmen, who do not have a teleport to the central isle and tend to attack by swimming across the river.

The forces of Undead grow daily. Why did I resist the truth for so long? My fellow Keepers now claim I am insane. They do not know; but they will. Story
Northern Trade Route
With Keepers searching the wilderness for assassins, this route is the surest way to the next conquest. I look forward to enslaving his cowardly race of decadents. No more will they plague the land with their nauseating music and cloying sweet liquor. I have promised my eager Goblin minions a dozen Halfling slaves each. Tired of slavery, my Goblins are eager to fight, but we must hurry. I've only 20 days to take the city Lunaris at the end of the Trade Route before my diversion is discovered and all opportunity of destroying the United Cities disappears.

Map features
Starting positions and cities

Walkthrough
Compared to the alternative option of the Subterranean Path, the main benefit of playing this map is that a second hero, Gorthak, can be acquired. The main drawback is that the alternative option provides a guaranteed item with
First Strike
. If Gorthak is missed, or is not carried over into the next map, the next opportunity to acquire a second hero will be in the map after the next map.
In this map, the player begins at the southwest corner of the map and must reach the city of Lunaris, which is located at the southeast corner, within 20 turns. Alternatively, this map can also be completed by defeating the Halfling leader (who is usually at the northeast corner) within 20 turns. Due to the turn limit, there is generally no time to develop cities. Similarly, conquering cities, unless incidental to exploration towards the destination, would also likely be detrimental to completing this scenario in time.
Lunaris can be reached simply by following the road. However, after crossing the first bridge to the north of the starting position, turn right (instead of following the road) to find Gorthak, who is found just north of the neutral city of Kurdem. Gortak will offer to join, along with two
Goblin Wolf Riders
.
Outcome
An Easy Triumph
My swift journey and the capture of Lunaris sent the pitiful Halflings scampering to their burrows. And yet, as we arrive, the Orc and Goblin forces languish in reluctance. The Orcs' many defeats have made them sluggish to fight in the sunlight. I can see it is time for me to take control of these forces. As other Stormlords cower, I delight in the upcoming conflict.
IN-GAME TEXT

Story
War on the Safelands
Frostlings, Orcs, and Dark Elves gather. Battle is imminent. The Cult has also convinced a group of greedy Lizardmen that the weakened Dwarves hoard a treasure. No doubt, they view the Safelands as a deathtrap. Steep mountain walls reflect urgency. If we do not prevail, the Dwarves will be trapped in the natural fortress without hope of escape. I've tried to convince the weaker to flee, but the Dwarves point out to me that they have no where else to go. The Dwarves believe holiness abides in the tops of these mountains, and refuse to surrender hope.
I have confirmed that Stormlord Melenis leads the Cult's army. She stirs her forces to shrill frenzy. All hope rests in holding the Safelands. Should we fall the Frostlings may be intimidated to join Meandor in the Valley of Wonders. Further, should Melenis be allowed to escape, the secret powers that she wields over the earth, and the details of her plan, will forever plague the Dwarves. Victory must, therefore, be complete and untempered by lenient restraint traditional among Keepers -ironically, just the type of battle a Dwarven berserker was born to fight.

Walkthrough
While the map's general layout is relatively straightforward, this map notably marks the debut of a King-level AI opponent (the Orcs) and contains numerous altars from which AI opponents may fire upon your forces.
Early on, it is advantageous to secure the independent cities to the east and west, including the area that is further east past the bridge, which includes a city, a farm, and a life node. Afterwards, defeating the Dark Elves is arguably the priority, since the Dark Elves have an easily accessible path to threaten the entire area east of the player's starting position, whereas attacks from the Orcs are more constricted to a single area.
After completing this scenario, the player must choose between supporting either the Elves or the Highmen, two separate paths that lead to different endgames.
Outcome
A New Home
The Dwarves blow trumpets of victory from every clime. The Frostlings melt away. The few surviving Orcs tremble at the sight of Dwarves. The lizards abandoned their lust for gold. The Dark Elves are vanquished. Melenis lies dead. The insane conviction in her eyes frightened me more than any weapon or earth-shattering spell. I once believed the Cult acted by chaotic cowardice, but now I see they intend to win this conflict no matter the cost to this world. Her reckless resentment leads me to believe no intelligence report we have received is exaggerated.
I fear the strange messages salvaged from Melenis' belongings indicate that terrible powers are about to wash over us all. I have sent warnings and news to Julia by Dwarven Balloon. Charged with the confidence over this victory, every Dwarf in the city enlisted to join Julia and the Keepers in the Valley of Wonders. Still, I refuse to condemn mothers, children and elderly to war, no matter how much they beg to join. They need warriors to guarantee they prosper, to rebuild, and to gather their scattered people, so I select but a few.
Life and Death
Three days ago, the white star changed to crimson. Julia sends word that our greatest fear infects the world again. Meandor has done the unspeakable, freeing Inioch from the grave in the form of walking-death. With the bloody star, the loss of their queen, and now the spread of pestilence which blights their verdant forest-lands, the Elves go to an island. From this "Isle of Last Goodbyes," they believe to sail to a mythical sanctuary called "Evermore." With the Elves leaving, who will stand against Meandor's slaughter, or the waves of death which consume the living earth?
An enigmatic race called Highmen has offered to combat the Undead. These beings of light scorch the Undead by sheer righteous dominion. I have seen little of their troops, save that where they strike, nothing evil remains. Still, I am cautious to empower such an unknown force. I know Julia would prefer that I choose to help her people migrate to their ships. But if I help the Elves leave, will some remain to take the Valley of Wonders? Or do I ally myself with these Highmen and leave the Elves to find their own course?
IN-GAME TEXT

The Skull
is the first scenario in the Undead route of the
campaign
in
Age of Wonders
, and the 8th scenario in the campaign overall if the Undead route was chosen. The Undead route is an option available in the
Cult of Storms
version of the campaign under all preceding routes, and is also available in the
Keepers
version of the campaign if the player previously assisted the Lizardmen.
Story
Main
Keepers
Cult of Storms
Select a campaign faction from the tabs above to view the corresponding text.
Fractured Skull
Forbidden thoughts haunt my mind. Inioch's whispers cannot be ignored. I am consumed by this carnal prison. I try to scream but can make no sound. I am truly alive. I see the truth in my being. Life is weak. All things die, but death is without end. Inioch has given me much and expects only that I gratify him him. I am hesitant to strike against the Keepers -my past life. I will be merciful. The enemy we share will be my target. I have not chosen to ally with Inioch's exalted children to punish the Keepers.
Dark Elves have long held "the Skull", a mountain of utmost sanctity. Once a shrine to Elven folk, the Dark Elves have defiled the place with their half-dead, squandering the powers of death. Inioch will be most pleased with my offering. Surely, if I succeed, he will bless me with the power to control the dark cravings that strangle me. I will have power to end all war. The mountain -this Skull- glows bright with the return of Inioch. I will deliver it to my Master's feet, and he will give me power. Then I will be free.
About the Undead
The Undead draw strength from the places of death. They are inherently resistant to fire, cold and lightning. They are not affected by death magic or poison. They are inherently superior in almost every way to the living. Hellhounds and other things demonic are frequently found within the confines of an Undead town. Undead fashion battering rams from the bones of their victims. Others who die by Undead hands are reborn as skeleton warriors and archers, and the dreaded death-knights.
IN-GAME TEXT (KEEPERS VERSION)
Blackened Skull
Meandor fled, leaving me to choose between Inioch and his cowardly son. Meandor claims that a mistake has been made. I will agree with him. A mistake has been made. That mistake was my allegiance to the wrong Master. The other Stormlords scramble to cover their fiefdoms, and hide from the powers of these new gods: the Undead. I will not be the one that grovels for his life when this engagement is over. Inioch has promised me dominion over all living creatures for the duration of this world. Ultimately, I decide who lives and who perishes.
I will finish the work abandoned by Meandor, and crush Humanity; but first, Inioch desires a place of power: A mountain called "the Skull." For centuries the Dark Elves have perfected their dark magic within this mountain. It is a sacred place of death, where Meandor learned the blackest arts, even those that brought Inioch back to the world. The Skull burns hot with the return of the Undead. It is befitting that Inioch should desire it for his necromancers. Should the Dark Elves resist, I will see their bones dance for their true king.
About the Undead
The Undead cannot be killed, for they are dead. Death affords them many advantages including immunities to poison, fear, charm, and death magic. They are resistant to cold, fire and lightning. Their otherworldly forces include demons, hellhounds, and the hosts of all that have died. They feed upon fear and turn mortal realms into graveyards. Death Knights gallop through nightmares riding the bones of hellish animals long deceased, while Doom Priests proclaim the end of the world. They move with one mind, spreading their black sleep across all the land unburdened by conscience or emotion.
IN-GAME TEXT (CULT VERSION)

Walkthrough
This map requires infiltrating the skull-shaped mountain at the center of the map in order to defeat the enemy. The conspicuous design of this formation makes finding the opponent straightforward. Note that there is a one-way teleport south of the Skull that enables the opponent to teleport troops to the north of the map.
Outcome
Main
Keepers

Select a campaign faction from the tabs above to view the corresponding text.
Visions of Chains
Inioch is pleased with my offering. He tempts me with perfection. He promises unquenchable power over all beings and I know they are true. I cannot disbelieve. I have no choice, but power. My will is drawn to Inioch. The Keepers send their warnings, pleading that I forsake this path. They do not understand. I will make them understand. I will chain their hearts as Inioch has chained mine. Chained in truth, they will taste the thing they fear and know the meaning in spite of life. But first, I will prove myself worthy of Inioch's grace.
IN-GAME TEXT (KEEPERS VERSION)
Power Hold
As I have promised, I have secured the desired holdings. Am I to be an executioner forever, or do I have a greater calling? I see how the Lizardmen flock to me, and the Goblins before them. Now that I am freed from Meandor's shadow, I begin to wonder. Here in the swamp, where things with large snapping teeth devour things with smaller snapping teeth, I am beginning to see life according to the true order of things. These lizards desire a competent leader, one willing to guarantee them luxuries. They desire a leader like me.

Story
Final Obstacle
I stand before the last pass to the Valley of Wonders ready to enter. What is this that stands before me? After insurmountable odds, a final force raises its hand against me. A law has been broken; I demand justice. They plea for mercy, while brandishing steel. After all else, the Highmen and Keepers join. They pledge their fealty to a banner stained crimson with the blood of all Elves. Their false idol of peace at any cost shall topple. Fate favors the Human scourge no longer. Their reward, oblivion, cannot be deferred by kind thoughts and weak minds.
IN-GAME TEXT
Map features
Starting positions and cities
Dark Elves
(player-controlled) - The player begins on an island in the southwest with the size 3 city Mohiam. The player is at war with four other good-aligned factions, which are all allied with one another against the player.
Highmen
(CPU Lord) - The Highmen begin with two cities, including the size 4 city Antobus, at the northwest bank of the river.
Elves
(CPU Lord) - The Elves begin with two cities that are separated by the river (but inter-accessible via a teleport pair), including the size 4 city Shellon located on the northeast bank of the river and protected by a large formation of holy ground.
Halflings
(CPU Lord) - The Halflings begin with two cities on the east bank of the river, including the size 4 city Tiprydd.
Dwarves
(CPU Lord) - The Dwarves begin with two cities, including the size 4 city Bellian on the southwest bank of the river and an additional city at the south section of the caverns level.

Altar of Life
- West of the Halfling's main starting city
Teleport
- At the southeast section of the caverns level. This teleport has its destination set to the water that is south of the Elves' starting city. For this reason, units that cannot travel on water cannot use the teleport.
Teleport pair
- There is a pair of teleports located at each shore of the river just before the river branches off at the center of the map. The two teleports transport to each other's position.
Teleport pair
- A pair of teleports links the Elves two starting cities, by teleporting to each other's position across the river

Walkthrough
This map has a large number of size 4 cities as well as secondary gold resources. The player begins on an island that is isolated from the CPU factions by land, but will likely come under attack by air and sea since the opposing factions collectively have a respectable amount of starting ships and flying units.
In order to complete this scenario, the player must defeat an alliance of four opposing factions; the one that is closet to the players is the Dwarves, who have a starting city in the south section of the caverns that is accessible by the cave entrance at the player's starting island.
Outcome
Victory!
The Keepers scattered, proving the Dark Elves superior again. The lines of Human defense have fallen into the Valley of Wonders. The final battle will be decided there, but I know the outcome. My sword thirsts for Human blood. We will see justice. The Dark Elves are ready. I receive word daily of more Stormlords falling by the sword. Dark Elf holdings continue to fall to the enemy, but it matters not. Only the Valley matters. The forces I have amassed will not fail Meandor, and once the Valley of Wonders is ours, retaking those older places will be trivial.
IN-GAME TEXT

The
tutorial
is an optional part of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders II: The Wizard's Throne
that teaches basic gameplay elements. The tutorial is part of the overall story of the campaign, and is set directly after the events of the opening cinematic. It portrays Merlin's training after arriving in
Evermore
under the tutelage of
Gabriel
.
Story
Heed my words Merlin, and you shall learn the path to the Wizard's Throne.  I, Gabriel, shall guide you, and give you the power to master each sphere of magic.
But first, you have much to learn and there is little time. Learn to gather sources of magical power. Let this mana flow through you. Allow it to inspire your mind and over time, you shall learn new spells.  Or if you choose, focus these energies inward, to learn skills of power.
The races of your world do not cooperate easily, but you will need them.  You must be sensitive to each group and balance their needs and demands with your own.
Do not be idle.  Teach your people to be industrious, build tools, fortifications, and structures of power.  Instruct them to expand over the face of the land. Lift them up, and they will help you expand your own domain by building monuments that enhance your abilities-even the greatest of all structures, the Wizard's Tower.
—Gabriel's opening monologue
Outcome
Well done, Merlin. You are ready to gather your people, and make them great again.  Remember the lessons you have learned here in Evermore. Treat all people and power with fairness.  Be patient and you shall prevail.  Find my renegade wizards.  Face them. Calm their fury. Bring them back to me. When you are tested sufficiently in a sphere of magic, return to me, and I will help you pass to the next sphere. Now go.  The world awaits the hero you must become.
—Gabriel's closing monologue
Quotes
This scenario includes multiple quotes from Gabriel that reveal information on the aspect of magic in the setting:
"
Magic is subdivided into six specific spheres and one general sphere.  Each of these spheres represents a certain aspect of the universe, ranging from the powers of death and life to raw elemental fury.
"
"
The energy of the spheres manifests itself through power nodes. They are the most important power source for wizards. Nodes typically generate 10 Power, but a Node of your specific sphere will generate 20 Power.
"
"
The wizards Artica the Ice Queen, and Tempest, Lord of the Skies, govern the sphere of Air.
"
"
The jolly merchant Marinus and the mysterious Nimue govern the sphere of Water.
"
"
The grumpy Fangir and the solitary Mab govern the sphere of earth.
"
"
Arachna the Spider Queen and the twisted Nekron govern the sphere of death.
"
"
The arrogant Yaka and Seductive Karissa govern the Sphere of Fire.
"
"
The ancient Serena and wise Anon are the wards of the sphere of Life.
"
"
What the six specific spheres do not cover, the broad Cosmos sphere encompasses.  While not as specifically directed as any of the other six spheres, the Cosmos sphere can cast spells of each sphere and many of its own useful spells of enchantment, alteration, and cancellation.
"
"
Cosmos unites all the spheres; mastering it is the ultimate goal in your quest. I, aged Gabriel, govern the sphere of Cosmos. With my wizards forsaking me, I have but little power left.
"

Keepers

Select a campaign faction from the tabs above to view the corresponding text.
Guilt and Excuses
My hope for reconciliation between Julia and me just died. Blaming Humanity for Elwyn's death, a group of Aldorian Elves is determined to destroy the Highmen before they build sufficient forces here. They have captured an assortment of powerful altars within Unicorn Valley that are capable of leveling cities. The Elves require time to heal, but we must move now. They must be expelled from the valley and the altars must be secured. To complicate matters, the unicorns will side with the Elves, as has always been their way. I doubt Julia will understand the need for this assault.
IN-GAME TEXT (KEEPERS VERSION)
Turnabout
Finally a mission worth doing, and Gabriel bores me with rationalizations. For aeons, the Highmen and Elves have coexisted in some form of symbiosis. They serve each other in some grand scheme. Snore. I care not for Elves. A few went crazy and wants to destroy us. I will destroy them, regardless of the unicorns protecting them in Unicorn Valley. The Elves are right to fear me and the Highmen. I assassinated their queen and now I use the Highmen to end this conflict in control. At least Gabriel will remain behind; I will be spared his excuses.

Outcome
Main
Keepers
Cult of Storms
Select a campaign faction from the tabs above to view the corresponding text.
Songs in Passing
Highmen sing dolorous hymns to the fallen. Beauty mixes with loss in perfect symbolism. I want to weep. I see the wounded Elves. Fallen. I am hollow. Gabriel says that the Elves and Highmen have long shared a special relationship in and out of this world. His people weep for every fallen Elf--the fairest of all kin. The Highmen have peculiar beliefs, but they do soothe my trembling. They act on a faith for which I can only hope to hope. They are gifted with bright visions, while I squint blindly in their world of light.
IN-GAME TEXT (KEEPERS VERSION)
Caterwaul
Highmen sing too much. If it isn't some noisy hymn of laud, it is a wailing funeral chorus. Don't they know I'm trying to sleep? They have mourned the loss of every fallen Elf. I had no choice. I didn't enjoy the slaughter, but it was necessary. Yet, they act as if they lost the war. Instead of celebrating, they douse themselves in ash and wear rags to denote the terrible times which they endure. Perhaps I should have chosen the Undead. Sure, they would have killed me, but at least they would do so in quiet.

United Cities
is the third scenario in the
Cult of Storms version
of the
campaign
in
Age of Wonders
, and the final scenario in the Goblins section of the campaign. The
Keepers campaign
also has a
corresponding scenario
of the same name and the same general map layout.
Story
Siege on United Cities
Justice rages against the idle Halfling race. As open allies with the Keepers, they must be punished most severely. Too long have they occupied the choice isles of the Inland Sea with no righteous ambitions save to annoy. Their capital city, Lyra, is the key to their fall. Without the capacity to recruit their more devious faerie-allies the Halflings will fail and flee. To the east tribes of Goblins amass the instruments of death and the scent of blood and smoke attracts blood-lusted Trolls and Orcs to join our siege.
IN-GAME TEXT
Map features
Starting positions and cities
Goblins
(player-controlled) - The player begins at the west side of the map with one city.
Halflings
(
CPU Knight
) - The Halflings begin at the center of the map with several cities, including the size 4 city Lyra, the capital of the United Cities.
Elves
(CPU Knight) - The Elves are allied with the Halflings and begin at the southwest part of the map with two cities, including the size 4 city Casfell.
Orcs
(CPU Squire) - The Orcs are allies and begin at at the southeast part of the map along with one city, the size 2 city Carkach.
Frostlings
(CPU Squire) - The Frostlings begin as a neutral and hold one city, the size 4 city Annelande, at the northeast part of the map.
Notable structures
Monster Lair
(low item value) - At the north part of the starting region (i.e., north of the first size 1 independent Halfling city)
Monster Lair
(low item value) - South part of the map between the Elf and Orc starting positions
Castle Ruin
(average item value) - South part of the map between the Elf and Orc starting positions
Heroes
CPU Leaders: Orag (Orcs), Esalan (Elves), Merwe (Halflings), Lord Thakor (Frostlings)
Walkthrough
This map presents an alliance vs. alliance scenario. The player has the benefit of being allied to the Orcs at the other side of the map. While the Orcs are at a lower CPU level than the Halflings and Elves, the east side of the map has a large number of independent settlements, making it possible for the Orcs to expand rapidly and provide substantial assistance to the player.
After completing this map, you must choose between the Orcs and the Lizardmen. This choice will have affect what endgame options are available later in the campaign.
Outcome
Vindication
How can I sleep, when I have to write of our glorious victory? Below me a chorus of sublime agony echoes through the shattered ruins of Lyra. The Halfling women shriek sweet music as my Goblin children take their reward-such jubilation from a race long subjected to slavery. In this victory our cause is proven just. This is the meaning of the star in the sky. This wound in the black night will close only by lancing that which festers across the realm.
As ravens blacken the battlefield, I must turn my attention to other scavengers. The Cult's Stormlords gather on the morrow to divvy up the spoils of my victory. The squabbling fools will ruin all I've done, if I allow them any crucial roles in Meandor's ploy. It will be difficult resisting the urge to have them all killed, but no, they can still be used, or at least their resources. I will be about the more important business of gathering an invincible army for Meandor. But truth is, I await for specific commands from Meandor, himself.
Secret Combination
For once, I am not left alone doing the Cut's work. Meandor's favorite wife, the Stormlord Melenis, devastated the Dwarven homeland of Deepmir with her earth sorcery. The perfect distraction! She planted rumors among the Frostlings, turning them against the Keepers. WIth the Lure of Dwarven gold and an easy kill, the Frostlings make unwitting pawns, further depleting the fleeing Dwarves. As a result I am compelled to leave the Frostlings to her, and while the predictable Keepers run off on missions of mercy to save their stunted friends, Melenis prepares her barbed snares.
"For not cost," the Lizardmen say they will back us. Still, lizards can be slippery. Meandor trusts the Orcs, but their tribes are in chaos. The lizards are strong, and in their native bogs, are unchallenged. Lizard realms border on Orc held positoins, should I choose lizards, it would strain the Cult's relations with the Orcs. Orcs are stupid--superstitious. If they are to be of any use to use, they need my tutelage. I have no doubt in Meandor's trust of my abilities to unite them, but I must select the surest path, and not just his favorite ally.
IN-GAME TEXT

United Cities
is the third scenario in the

in
Age of Wonders
, and the final scenario in the Halflings section of the campaign. The
Cult of Storms campaign

Story
The United Cities
Our path ahead is clear. Here we will stand against Meandor's Orcs and Goblins. Here we will create a future for our allies. If the Keepers are to gain any future allies, we will need to demonstrate that we can protect them. There are many that watch us and diplomatic pressure grows. Lord Thakor of the Froslings observes from the North, intent upon claiming sizable portions of Halfling lands. While not of the Cult, these opportunists must either enter an alliance or submit to Halfling sovereignty. Our only ally is a clan of wood elves, who dwell within the southwestern forests.
The capital city, Lyra, on the central island, is under siege. Even from Lunaris, across the Inland Sea, greasy black smoke streaks the sky. Assault fires mar the otherwise verdant isles. The fires are fed by Goblin and Orc swarms living to the east. It is clear that if Lyra falls, our cause will falter, thus I am imploring all those in my command to reach this central city as quickly as is feasible. Once safe, Lyra will serve a fine stronghold to secure the entire region.
IN-GAME TEXT
Map characteristics
Starting positions and cities
Halflings
(player-controlled) - The player begins at the west side of the map with one city.
Elves
(
CPU Squire
) - The Elves are allies and begin at the southwest part of the map.
Orcs
(CPU Knight) - The Orcs begin as a hostile opponent at the southeast part of the map along with two cities, including the size 4 city Carkach.
Goblins
(CPU Knight) - The Goblins begin as a hostile opponent at the east part of the map along with two cities, including the size 4 city Ospardec. The Goblins also begin with four
Goblin Wyvern Riders
at the west side of the map.
Frostlings
(CPU Squire) - The Frostling are neutrals to all other factions and hold one city at the start, the size 4 city Annelande, at the northeast part of the map.
Notable structures
Monster Lair
(low item value) - At the north part of the starting region (i.e., north of the first size 1 independent Halfling city)
Monster Lair
(low item value) - South part of the map between the Elf and Orc starting positions
Castle Ruin
(average item value) - South part of the map between the Elf and Orc starting positions
Heroes
CPU Leaders: Orag (Orcs), Esalan (Elves), Rolar (Goblins), Lord Thakor (Frostlings)
Walkthrough
The Halfling cities in the central island are neutral, but will join your forces with a payment of gold. Therefore, acquiring the Halfling cities and forces there, especially the central city of Lyra, is a top priority. If you reach and acquire Lyra before the enemy, the city garrison includes a
Halfling Eagle Rider
.
Eagles are extremely useful in this map because they enable you to easily reach the farmlands to the northeast. Note also that there are three
Transport Ships
in the canals of the center island, and one
Dragon Ship
at the shipyard by the farmlands. These boats will all offer to join you upon contact, and can be easily reached using eagles. Eagles also enable you to deal with the Goblins' Wyvern Riders that will likely harass your cities at the starting region.
After acquiring the Halfling cities in the middle, this map turns into a standard game against multiple opponents. The allied Elf player will assist, but is typically not as strong as the Orc and Goblin opponents. In the absence of diplomatic efforts, the Frostlings will typically not ally with you, in which case they will need to be defeated as well.
After completing this map, you must choose between the Dwarves and the Lizardmen. This choice will have affect what endgame options are available later in the campaign.
Outcome
Beckoning Star
It is near dawn and the celebrations are still ongoing; I cannot sleep, so I write. Despite the victory and jubilant crowds below, from this balcony, all I see is a flare fixed over the distant Valley. The bright star speaks my name, reminding me that there are greater forces at work. Julia sent congratulations at our victory via Eagle Riders. But with that praise comes disturbing news. Rumors abound that the Cult's necromancers plot to resurrect Lord Inioch. I fear Meandor, obsessed with obliterating humanity, tampers with seductive forces beyond any living being's control.
Perhaps these Halflings are mere scapegoats for why I cannot sleep. Perhaps I should join them again, with their twanging zithers and shrill pan flutes, their bubbling kettles and sweet wine, until I am too tired and groggy to contemplate the darkness that lurks on the horizon. I am thankful these little ones are here, their wisdom far exceeds their stature, smiling to the very end. On the morrow, a council of Keepers and allies gather to consider Julia's news and our next move. Perhaps then I shall know better, what path to follow.
Lyra Council
I have dire news. As the Keepers hoped to explore diplomatic ties with the Lizardmen and Frostlings, tragedy struck our allies in Deepmir. Collapsed is the vast underground nation belonging to the Dwarves. Vulnerable to extinction, the Dwarves must abandon our cause to salvage the remains of their people. Now we are faced with the question of pursuing new allies or aiding those ancient ones. Most of the Keepers insist we owe the Dwarves our assistance, but in our insistence upon charity, are we dooming ourselves?
Frostling arbitrations are frozen. They frigidly view the tragedy as a Keeper failure. Furthermore, because the Dwarven realm borders the Frostlings, they claim any migration to safety to be an act of war. The Lizardmen eye the Halflings hungrily, but assert a desire to help, if properly rewarded. Julia has expressed doubts that a lizard alliance would be affordable by Keeper standards. Still, their faces are most impressive, and a diplomatic mission might curb their appetites. The Lizard's realm is en route to the Valley of Wonders, and their forces, if organized, appear unbeatable.
IN-GAME TEXT

Uniting the Clans
is the first scenario in the Orc route in the
Cult of Storms version
of the
campaign
in
Age of Wonders
, and the fourth scenario in the campaign overall. This and other scenarios in the Orc route are available only if the player chose to help the Orcs following the events of
United Cities
.
Story
Civil Squalor
While Meandor assumes the Orcs will join us, I know them. The Orc legions promise obedience with drooling mouths, but exude an odor of rebellion. I, alone, can bridle these chaotic creatures. Orcs understand but one language: War. The realm is in chaos. Stormlords have displaced hosts of Dwarves, while Azracs, seeing the chaos, invade Orc territories to the south. Instead of repelling the invading forces, the Blackfist and Deadclaw clans fight amongst themselves. I will put an end to these squabbling forces, and hone the Orc legions into the Cult's weapon of vindication.
About the Orcs
Orcs are loathsome, foul creatures, living for the taste of blood. Their strength is unparalleled, but they are stubborn servants hearkening to carnal lusts. Even Orc women may serve as ferocious fighters. The smallest tribal gatherings employ deadly warriors, archers and machines for battering. Kobolds inhabit Orc settlements, shuffling through their garbage mounds. While Shamans curse their shredder-bolt ballista javelins, to deliver nasty wounds. Heavily armored warlords charge into battle, flashing their two-handed swords about with deadly accuracy.

Walkthrough
This map plays as a standard multi-sided free-for-all with a relatively simple map layout. Note that Azracs have a neutral good/evil alignment, which helps with maintaining stability of conquered Azrac cities when playing as the Orcs.
If the player starts this map without a second hero, the level 3 Orc hero Sister Tersia will be offered for recruitment immediately at the start of the map without requiring hero emergence. Sister Tersia comes with
Life Stealing
, an
ability
that is ordinarily only available in
leader customization
and rarely found among heroes recruitable in the campaign, making her a unique option as a second hero.

I have achieved my real design: Not the spoils of conquest, but a nation consumed with bloodlust! Under the flag of the Cult, Orc stomachs grumble greedily anticipating the next kill. Now I learn that the century-old Bormac Orcbane, a Dwarven hero freed from a Cult trap, has caused the Goblin laborers to revolt and threatens to disrupt my passage through the Ashen Steppes. I will secure both regions.

Upon the Rocks of Sacrifice
is the third scenario in the Elves route of the
Keepers campaign
and the 10th scenario in the campaign overall if this route was chosen.
Story
Upon the Rocks of Sacrifice
Tollrock Wood is the last obstacle to reaching the ancient shipyards, from which the journey should be simple. The Elven settlements around the edges of this forest are ripe with talk of evil prowling these woods. Tollrock is said to be a sacred and fearsome place, where Elven refugees two centuries in the past, fleeing the Human invasion, tried to escape via the shipyards. Some Elves say the land was barren, until the massacre began, and for every fallen Elf, up grew a tortured tree. The Elves hid in the clefts of the rocks, but nothing would stay the Human onslaught. None escaped.
When the wind blows, the Elves claim to hear the screams of their deceased comrades still echoing through the woods. Out of guilt, both Aldor and Silvanus tended the woodlands for decades, but no Elf dared venture underground. Instead, they patrolled the surface, guaranteeing passage to the shipyards. Now, however, all contact with the shipyards has been cut off. This dreary place would serve Undead most handily, and I fear respect for the dead has given the creatures a fine hunting ground. I intend to clear the way to the shipyards and rid this place of Undead.

Walkthrough
Expanding as quickly as possible to the cities at the center of the map (and to resources such as the Life Node west of the starting position) will be  beneficial, especially since the player begins with little and is faced with two AI-controlled opponents that begin with multiple cities. This scenario requires defeating both of them; fortunately, this task is made easier by the fact that both opponents will also be at war with one another.

Launching Point
The Tollrock shipyards were not held by Undead, as I had previously suspected, but by Dark Elves. Furthermore, the shipyards have been used. I fear for the Isle of Last Goodbyes. The Cult, more than any other, fears the power of Evermore. Some say it is the only thing which can cure their corrupted souls, and for that reason they fear it. With the Undead cast from the Elven forests, the true enemy is clear. But this last desperate move, may have exposed this enemy's weakness, and may provide us with a lasting solution to the Dark Elves' anger.

Meandor Scenario 2: Urland Fields
is the second scenario in Meandor's section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders: Shadow Magic
.
Story
Farms and mills line the fields of the Urland, now the rapidly expanding agricultural heart of the Phobian Empire. But this wasn't always so; this land used to be all swamp and jungle, where giant lizards roamed. They now raid the land that was once their home.
Meandor, before you teach your Larvae to call you "father", let us first strike a blow against Phobius. Six heroes, once loyal to the rising Queen Julia, have met to make a grab for her power. They are funded by Phobius, and hide in his richest lands, plotting Queen Julia's assassination. Her popularity has grown to legendary status, but she refuses to use the power to reinstate the old ways of privilege and royal favors.
While Phobius treats these traitors to obscene luxury, I think it is time her elder brother stepped out of the shadows to show what comes of the old ways. Slay the six conspirators. Show Phobius the fate of those who tangle with a Wizard of Death.
—Merlin's intro
Map features
Wizards
Meandor (player)
Ambir (CPU Squire)
Phobius (CPU King)

Ancient Ruin (item: Demon Mask) - North of the player's starting position

Heroes
Nielduh (Orc Rogue) - Traitor hero; does not have any starting items
Cordian (Archon Ranger) - Traitor hero; carries Thunder Shield and Ring of Willpower
Kaskar (Draconian Rogue) - Traitor hero; carries Venom Stinger
Winger (Halfling Rogue) - Traitor hero; carries Sword of Light, Platemail of Light, and Shield of the Ankh
Karzen (Tigran Warrior) - Traitor hero; carries Piercer, Dragon Helm, and Ring of Protection
Bowen (Dark Elf Paladin) - Traitor hero; carries Sacrificial Dagger, Thunder Armor, and Spider Totem
Tsi Iri (Draconian Shaman) - Given to Meandor if an alliance is made with Ambir
Walkthrough
This map is completed by killing the six traitor heroes, all of whom are part of Phobius' faction except for Kaskar, who is independent. Most of these heroes carry items, which can be used to boost your own heroes. The heroes closest to the player's starting position are Nielduh, who is just northeast of the starting city, and Winger, who is located at the Inn just further northeast. These two heroes, along with Kaskar and Bowen, have fixed locations or areas at which they are encountered. Kaskar is is located at the Dragon's Lair at the southeast part of the map, and Bowen is located at the Dungeon in the northeast part of the map. Karzen and Cordian are free-roaming, but are typically encountered in the center or northwest part of the map.
As the scenario progresses, Ambir will offer to work with you against Phobius, explaining that the latter has reneged on his promise to grant land.  If you make peace with Ambir, either through the diplomacy interface or by arriving at her main city, she will give you the Draconian hero Tsi Iri, who is out to hunt Kaskar. (Note: If you go to war with Ambir, due to an oversight in the scenario's design, you will not receive Tsi Iri even if you make peace with her later on.)
Once all six traitors have been defeated, the scenario ends on the following turn.
Outcome
Well done! Phobius' assassins are no more, and his tricks of deceit and intimidation have failed him. The ancient races withdraw their support in favor of the bright Elf Queen that fights with her people on the frontlines of the battlefields.
While Phobius continues to flee and hide behind great walled fortresses, churning up hate and fear to motivate the people, Queen Julia stands stalwart against the invaders.  Thanks to your efforts, she remains safe. Phobius's plot is spoiled.  The moldering bodies of his traitorous heroes shall nourish the crops of Urland field.
—Merlin's outro
Notable quotes
“
Death is but a portal to the Archon. Your actions here are vain. Liars have told you many lies to dissuade you, now I will speak truth.
Your father betrayed the Covenant prior to the advent of Humanity.  What you hate--these Humans.  You fight them, but they will inherit this earth.  And because your father refused to leave, they will inherit this world, forever cynical of the ancient ways of magic.
The powers that drove the creation of this sacred realm will dwindle and fade, whether or not you win here and now. That is why I fight for Phobias.  The end is inevitable, the dictator Phobias is mortal, he will die in a generation, at the very most, but your sister threatens to plunge this world into more death and destruction by preserving the old law.  That law was broken. Salvation doth not come by the law, it can only come in He who comes... in the Age of Men.  That is the key.  Humans must survive.
I don't matter.  It is the Humans...  preserve them and you may preserve your soul.
— Cordian's last words

Valley of Wonders
is the final scenario in all paths of the
Age of Wonders
single player
campaign
. It depicts the forces of the Elves, the Dark Elves, the Highmen, and the Undead all converging on the Valley of Wonders, the original site of the Elven court before the Valley fell under Human control.
Scenario variants
There are four versions of this scenario for purposes of gameplay, and a total of six total possible story variants. Depending on choices made during the campaign, the player will control either the Elves, the Dark Elves, the Highmen, or the Undead, with the first two being exclusive to the
Keepers campaign
and the
Cult of Storms campaign
, respectively. The Highmen and Undead paths endgame are possible in both campaigns but have different story texts for the two campaigns.
Internally, there are four map files for this scenario, one for each of the four possible endgame factions. The four map files differ mainly as to the faction that is controlled by the human player. The rest of the map, including the units, structures, and geographical features, is essentially the same. The Highmen and Undead versions have different respective story texts depending on whether the overall campaign is with the Keepers or the Cult, but the map file that is used for purposes of gameplay is the same in both cases.
Story
Main
Elves
Undead (Keepers)
Highmen (Keepers)
Dark Elves
Undead (Cult)
Highmen (Cult)
The story text depends on the endgame race and campaign. Select one of the tabs to view the story text for the corresponding campaign and race.
The Valley of Wonders
Julia is here, and our reunion has been a joyful one. She sees beyond weaponry with a rare vision. She speaks little of the mission that lies ahead. Instead, she winks knowingly at me, and talks only of victory. She smiles soothingly when I voice my fears. The mission is simple. We must conquer any and all who stand against us. Only then, can we establish order. Inioch's ruined court lies in the center of the valley. Nearby lay the Human settlements, and around them, lay all other factions. It is here that we stand for all that matters.
IN-GAME TEXT
The Valley of Wonders
My Halfling allies draw back in fear, but I am beyond their trivial concerns. Julia held a funeral in my behalf. Do not mourn for me, my dear ones. Soon you shall know the freedom that comes from death. Inioch has promised to free me from the burden of breath, and grant me unstoppable power after this last engagement within the Valley of Wonders. With that power, I will free you. Is this not what you desire? True peace comes only in shedding mortality. Come and fear not. As you are, I once was; I am, what you will be.
IN-GAME TEXT
The Valley of Change
Behold! The Valley of Wonders. I should have ignored the message, but Julia was a friend. Her message was simple and short. Gabriel is not pleased that I would seek such a distraction before this great engagement. Julia desires that I return to them, and they will forgive me. I had not planned to return until after the battle but Gabriel's reaction was of such judgement that I actually found myself contemplating it. For a people believing in freedom, the Highmen can be strictly intolerant at times. Still, I know that I cannot go back now.
The Keepers would lock me away in some scholar's tower to study an ancient mystery. I will not be shut out of this final conflict. No, I will remain until the end. Only I know the Highmen. Perhaps I can keep the Keepers from wasted hostility. Evil must be our only target. Gabriel will be here too. He says that he must fight if he is to be exalted. He acts as though he might die, or that death is part of his exaltation. I choose to stay and see that he remains safe, and that evil is vanquished forever.
IN-GAME TEXT
Valley of Wonders
For over a century, the Humans have infested the Valley of Wonders. Yet they are ignorant fools, unschooled in any of the true powers. Much of Inioch's court and its secrets remain untouched. Inioch leads the Undead. Julia leads the Keeper forces. Other races come in small numbers to see if they might acquire some fortune. But none will stop my children, the Goblins; my swords, the Orcs; my power, the Dark Elves; and my flag, Meandor. I will be victorious. It is written across the bloody star.
IN-GAME TEXT
Valley of Wonders
All my allies are here. It is good to be among the living as well as these potent Undead. Their numbers grow quickly and Inioch is anxious to reestablish his court. Near the center of the Valley lay the ruined remains of the court. There will be plenty of Human settlements to feed upon, plenty of spoils for my living allies as well. I am told that Meandor is here, but he is nothing. Julia's forces will likewise fold against our power. And Humanity will know blessed servitude to Undead masters.
IN-GAME TEXT
Valley of Opportunity
Meandor sends assassins and bribes to stop me. Neither have worked. I can forego the bribes, for when this battle is over I will have sufficient arms and power to walk into the Dark Elf capital and pocket their treasury. The Highmen care nothing of gold and are liberal with their possessions. Gabriel goes on and on about the evils of war and how this battle is a necessity. He states that the Highmen would not kill if it could be justly avoided, then he gives me his sword and expects me to fight. I will never understand the Highmen.
The battle which follows is pivotal. So much so that Gabriel fights among us. He says that he must fight if he is to be "exalted." I don't know if that means he thinks he will die, or even if that matters. All the races and factions are here. The Keepers are gathered under Julia. The Undead follow Inioch's whims. And Meandor hides among his minions. But I am at the center, for I am with the Highmen, here to protect the fledgling race known as Humans. Before us lies the end of a legend and the start of glory.
IN-GAME TEXT
Layout and structures
This map has a central island surrounded by multiple surrounding regions, most of which are separated from each other by a river. Additionally, the caverns level features a circular path that provides an alternative route to travel between the surrounding regions (but not the central island).
Factions and starting positions, heroes, and cities
The player will control one of the four endgame factions, with the remaining three being controlled by the computer at the CPU King level.
Elves
- The Elves start at the northeast region of the map with 3 four-hex cities: Tuckawan (Elves), Telmshire (Halflings), and Bjoren (Dwarves). The Dark Elves begin at war with the Undead and the Dark Elves, but are neutral with the Highmen and Humans.

Undead
- The Undead start at the northwest region of the map with 3 four-hex cities, one of which is the Undead city Gharvas. If you are not playing as the Undead, the two other cities will also be Undead cities. If you are playing as the Undead, the other two cities have variable races that depend on which factions you played as during the first and second part of the campaign, i.e., Halflings and Lizardmen in the Keepers campaign, and Goblins and Orcs/Lizardmen in the Cult campaign. The Undead begin at war with all other factions except the Dark Elves, who are neutral.
