The special story characters (Julia, Meandor, Gabriel, and Lord Inioch) have slightly different abilities and stats depending on which version of the map is played (note that the hero data given above are for the versions in which they appear on the player's side). Walkthrough
The Humans begin as by far the strongest side due to having the most starting cities, access to a large amount of gold resources (which is significantly augmented by the Emperor CPU level), and several
air galleys
as starting units. Due to the air galleys, it is very possible for the Humans to defeat either the Undead or Dark Elves (or both) early on, since CPU leader stacks often lack effective countermeasures against air galleys.
In the Highmen version of this scenario, the Humans will assist as allies and do not need to be defeated. In the three other versions, the player must defeat all other factions on the map, including the Humans. This task will likely require effective utilization of the player's main hero (and any secondary heroes) developed during the previous maps of the campaign.
Heroes focusing on combat attributes and abilities can become decisively strong on this map, especially with the benefit of bonuses from
items
, which CPU heroes do not acquire. Often, the most practical way to fight a strong CPU faction is to directly hunt the enemy leader by sending a single strong hero or stack that can withstand all enemy forces while moving through enemy territory. In the case of the Humans, their leader is most commonly found in the underground section at the center of the map. Successfully capturing the center island will make all remaining opponents relatively easy, since the center has a huge amount of resources along with five size-4 human cities, all of which can be used to produce air galleys. Air galleys can easily cross the water, and a single galley can often defeat entire CPU stacks.
In all versions of this map, the Undead and Elves can easily access each other's territory through the cross-river teleports; the same situation applies to the Highmen and Dark Elves. These teleports make it a priority to either defeat the cross-river opponent early on or, alternatively, station a strong stack at the teleport terminal to block off potentially incoming enemy troops.
Elf version
Compared to the Dark Elf and Undead versions, the Elf version of this scenario provides the player with a substantial advantage in not being at war with the Humans at the beginning. The Elves also begin with a
Galleon
at a shipyard far isolated from the action at the center. Ironically, the combination of these two perks enable the player to prepare a sneak attack on the Humans, such as with a landing squad suitable to head straight to the center underground city.
If you invested in four spheres of Life magic, Julia's level V spell casting can be used to quickly summon a few
Gold Dragons
, which are practical on this map due to the large abundance of power sources. A stack that includes well-built campaign heroes, Julia, and one or more Gold Dragons would likely be able to take the center of the map with ease.
Dark Elf version
The Dark Elf version is somewhat more challenging than the Elf one, since the player is adjacent to two hostile factions, including the Humans, who will typically send their air galleys against the Dark Elves. As a result, when playing as the Dark Elves, you will be encountering hostile forces very early on.
Undead version
The Undead version requires the player to face three adjacent enemies right from the beginning. On the other hand, a player for the Undead gets the benefit of having Inioch as a hero, who is arguably by far the most powerful and best built of all of the special story heroes. With 10 defense, 7 attack, Extra Strike, Death Strike, and Regeneration, Inioch is very well built for melee combat, in addition to being a maximum rank spellcaster.
Compared to the Elves and Dark Elves, the Undead do not enjoy neutral relations with the Humans. However, due to the heavy presence of Human settlement on the map, it may be worthwhile (ironically, when considering the story) to improve relations with humans in order to better utilize their cities. Even without good relations with humans, air galleys are still useful because they are mechanical, and do not suffer from morale issues relating to race relations.
Highmen version
Since the Highmen are allied with the Humans, this version of the scenario is by far the easier, likely easier than most other scenarios in the whole campaign. The Humans will assist you in defeating the Undead and Dark Elves, sometimes accomplish both feats entirely on their own early in the map. The Humans are not at war with the Elves initially. However, once the player goes to war with the Elves, the Human will, in most cases, also end up going to war with the Elves even without the player's further intervention.
Outcome
Main article:
Campaign endings (Age of Wonders)
Gallery
The ruins of the Elven Court in the Valley of Wonders, as depicted in this scenario

Water Sphere, Episode 1
is the first scenario in the Water Sphere section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders II: The Wizard's Throne
.
Story
I feel within me the motion of the seas. Gabriel has endowed me with the power of Water.
The humans talk fearfully of the vicious Goblin hordes. Out of desperation they have chosen to bow down to a cruel water goddess named Nimue. She demands the people sacrifice their fair daughters to prove their loyalty to her. Gabriel informs me that Nimue is a wizard, whose vanity and envy is legendary, even within the Circle. We shall see.
The wizard Marinus used to hold this land, but his Halfling followers have no mind for war.  Marinus is greatly weakened and has asked for Gabriel's help. He claims he cannot return to Evermore by his own power.
The Halflings are savvy tradesmen and could provide my colonies with commerce, but wresting the minds of my fellow humans free from Nimue's embrace will be difficult.
—Merlin's opening monologue
Map features
Wizards
Merlin
- The player beings at the southwest island with no cities
Marinus
(CPU Squire) - Marinus is allied to the player and has cities on the southeast island, which is connected to the player's starting island by teleport
Mab
(CPU Knight) - Mab has cities throughout the map, including three cities on the mainland, including the surface
Nimue
(CPU Knight) - Nimue has multiple cities on the mainland, and is allied with Mab against the Merlin and Marinus
Notable structures
Magic Vault
- On the starting island, northwest of Merlin's starting position
Haunted crypt
- On the west part of the landmass northeast of the starting island, near a sign that says, "Here rests the king of Waterdown" (Waterdown being the razed town nearby)
Haunted Crypt
- On the southeast part of landmass northeast of the starting island
Ancient Ruin
- At the northeast corner of the map, near Nimue's main starting city
Items
The cave in Marinus' island has an item lying on the ground
The cave in the northeast section of the underground has an item on the water at the south end
Heroes
Winger
(Halfling warrior) - Starting hero for Marinus
Taberu
(Human ranger - Starting hero for Nimue
Avernus
(Elf rogue) - Eligible to emerge; typically, one of either Avernus or Lilly will likely offer to join Merlin, while the other will likely join Marinus
Lilly
(Halfling ranger) - Eligible to emerge
Petrog
(Goblin warrior) - Eligible to emerge
Dragor
(Draconian warrior) - Eligible to emerge
Jack
(Undead rogue) - Eligible to emerge
Walkthrough
The player starts with no cities, but can gain the independent halfling city to the east on the starting island. The starting island also has a city controlled by Mab just southeast of the halfling city. This city is is very lightly defended and can be taken on the second turn. Capturing it is a priority; otherwise, Marinus may take it himself, which will limit the player's growth in the beginning. Marinus is ally against Mab and Nimue, but his activity will be generally limited to his and Merlin's starting islands.
This particular scenario has a peculiar setup that makes a slow build-up strategy viable. Since the player starts on an island and CPU players do not attack across water using transport ships, you can take as much time as needed to build up on the starting island and on Marinus' island without being attacked by any substantial force. It is possible to build additional cities on Marinus' island to bolster your economy until you have sufficient forces to attack Mab and Nimue on the mainland.
Alternatively, instead of building up slowly on the two islands, a rapid-expansion approach could focus on securing the mainland right after taking Mab's city on the starting island. In particular, capturing the city of Williston near the center of the map, which has a pre-built wizard tower, will secure a strong foothold on the mainland. The main difficulty of attacking early is that Mab and Nimue will have large forces on the mainland, thus potentially requiring the player to fight strong forces early on.
Outcome
Now that I have freed the Halflings from the tyranny of Nimue and the Goblins, the Halflings are anxious to meet new friends across the seas.
Marinus has troubling news. His tower in Evermore was taken by a conspiracy of wizards within the Circle, acting to conceal their actions from Gabriel. Without his tower, he is trapped here.  Marinus believes the conspiracy's actions are two-fold: to gather power in this land, and use it to gain greater power in Evermore.
—Merlin's closing monologue

Story
The Halflings are ready to sail, but the Serpent River remains an obstacle.  Without free passage, the tiny ships will never reach the seas to the south and my colonies beyond. I must control this waterway.
Gabriel reaffirmed what Marinus reported.  A mystic darkness obscures Marinus's tower in Evermore, and it is spreading.  As it expands, Gabriel loses dominion in Evermore. Gabriel wants me to track down the conspirators who plotted against Marinus before their ambition overpowers other realms.
—Merlin's opening monologue

Wazz

Walkthrough
This is a large and complex map with several other wizards, and will likely require slowly pushing outward and controlling a large portion of the map in order to win. Some of the other wizards can become your allies, namely Anon (who will offer peace right at the beginning), Fangir, and Karissa. If you ally with multiple wizards, those other wizards must also ally with each other in order for you to win by allied victory. If multiple wizards allied to you fail to ally with each other, it will be necessary to defeat one or more of them.
Outcome
The first fleet of Halfling ships is away!  Nimue's influence has dwindled and the humans can now live free from her terror.
The alliance between Nimue and Nekron is troubling, though. Neither wizard would admit their true reasons for their alliance.  They act as gods, expecting reverence, and claim their only desire is to restore balance. Then they rend the lands and flood the earth with cataclysms. Gabriel still suspects a conspiracy, but all I see is madness.
—Merlin's closing monologue

Water Sphere, Episode 2
is the optional third scenario in the Water Sphere section of the
campaign
of
Age of Wonders II: The Wizard's Throne
.
Story
Centuries ago, an eccentric halfling gave an island to the Elves.  The Elves, battered from the loss of their Wizard-King Inioch and their Valley of Wonders, flourished upon this island, named Aldor. Inioch's daughter Julia later led the Elves back to reclaim the Valley, abandoning Aldor. The island fell to darkness. Now the Halflings want me to reclaim it.
I admit I am intrigued by the prospect to explore a place which once hosted Julia, before she ascended to be Queen in the Valley of Wonders.
—Merlin's opening monologue

Jattah
(Goblin rogue) - Starting hero for Mab
Walkthrough
Mab is a King-level opponent and has forces throughout the main island. However, the player has the advantage of heroes carried over from the previous scenario.
This scenario has a secret area that is accessible by repairing the lighthouse at the northeast corner of the map. Repairing the lighthouse a pioneer, which can reach the lighthouse by water-traversal spells such as Liquid Form and Water Walking. Once the lighthouse is repaired, it becomes a teleport into the secret area. Leaving the secret area requires finding two "Eye" items. The hero Jam (who uses the same portrait as
Ham
) is encountered in the area.
Outcome
The halflings have returned to Aldor. It will again flourish under their care. My people will also benefit from this good deed. The island provides another safe port of call.
But I must forget the visions of Julia's old home, and concentrate upon Gabriel's quest.  Only by mastering all the spheres of magic will I be able to restore lasting order and balance to this land.
—Merlin's closing monologue

Wizard College
is the second scenario in the Elves route of the
Keepers version
of the campaign in
Age of Wonders
, and the 9th scenario in the campaign overall if this route was chosen.
Story
Help From a Friend
A Dwarf who fought with me in the Safelands, named Moljnir, has sent word to me. He tells of a Wizard's college willing to teach me and the Elves, a powerful new spell, which allows the opening of stable transport gates, across the world. If this is true, the Elven journey could be completed without peril and in an instant. I have followed Moljnir's instructions, though some are strange. He insists that I must not bring a large armed force, because the wizards of the college are skittish. Still, I refuse to come defenseless.
The details of Moljnir's message are beyond the talent of a forger, and the lockbox was genuine Dwarven-make, but I struggle to quell my doubts. Skittish wizards with a spell to solve all my problems? As instructed, I've come to the hamlet of Sugarwood, but I've yet to see Moljnir. On the morrow, I'm to proceed to the wizard's college, following the signs. All questions will be answered, at least according to Moljnir's message. I should be excited, so why can't I dismiss the dread in my gut, the nagging doubts which strangle my optimism?
IN-GAME TEXT
Map features
Starting positions and cities
Elves
(player-controlled) - The player begins at the southwest part of the map with the size 3 city Sugarwood
Goblins
(
CPU Lord
) - The opponent holds no cities and is led by
Melenis
, the antagonist of the Dwarven part of the campaign who was supposedly killed during the events of
The Safelands
. Although Melenis is an Undead hero (and former Dark Elf), this map has the race of the opposing faction set to Goblins.

(average value items) - West of the player's starting city

(provides

and

West tower - Level 3 Earth, Air, Cosmos, or Special spell
North tower - Level 4 spell of any sphere
Northeast tower - Level 3 spell of any sphere except Death and Fire
East tower - Level 3 spell of any sphere except Death and Fire

Heroes
Sondra the Priestess
- Free hero (Dwarf hero)
CPU Leaders: Melenis (Goblins faction, Undead hero)
Walkthrough
This map has no active opposition since the opposing faction has no cities, and only has non-exploring stacks. Therefore, you may take as long as you like to complete the scenario without being under any threat. To complete the scenario, travel down to the caverns near the wizard towers and defeat Melenis. Three of the opponent's stacks are set to
guard area
and will attack when you venture close to the cave entrances.
Outcome
Treachery's Relase
Melenis is dead, again. I doubt I will ever forget her horrible face. I cannot believe I could be drawn into her trap so easily. The wizards of the college were grateful to be rescued, but the spell promised by my possessed friend never existed. Still, I have my life, and I confess gratitude for the lessons I've learned here. The Elves in Silvanus are moving out, and the path through the wildwood is treacherous. Rather than couch my hopes in miraculous mirages, I suppose the Elves will need to complete this journey by means of hard labor.
IN-GAME TEXT
Gallery
The Wizard College
Notes
The plot of this scenario is explained in the Undead route of the
Cult of Storms campaign
. According to the outcome narrative for
The Isle of Burbatak
and the introduction narrative for
Opposition
,
Inioch
resurrected Melenis, but the Stormlord serving Inioch is displeased of her undead form and thus sends her to assassinate the Keeper who killed her. The story texts also mention the use of a captured Dwarven hero as a means to lure the Keeper.
